Ruling on Sewn Garments for Muhrim and Definition of Ka'bayn
Ruling on wearing khuff for muhrim and defining ka'bayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sewn garments for a muhrim, identify the exception for khuff, and distinguish the two Hanafi interpretations of ka'b in the context of ihram.

Core Idea
A muhrim may only wear khuff if unable to find sandals, and must cut them below the instep—not the ankle.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the prohibition of sewn garments during ihram, based on the hadith of Ibn Umar. The exceptional permission for khuff is conditional, and the definition of ka'b (the point below which the khuff must be cut) is subject to an important intra-Hanafi difference. Understanding this distinction prevents misapplication of the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited garments and the general ruling
From the hadith, list the explicitly prohibited sewn items (shirts, trousers, turbans, hooded cloaks, khuff). Note that the general ruling is prohibition for the muhrim.
The prohibition is general, covering all sewn garments that are worn typically.
2
Locate the exception for khuff and its conditions
The hadith provides an exception: if one lacks sandals, he may wear khuff provided they are cut below the ka'bayn. Identify the two conditions: (1) absence of sandals, (2) cutting below ka'bayn.
The exception is specific to khuff, not any other garment.
3
Define ka'b as used in this context
The commentary presents two interpretations of ka'b: (1) the ankle bones, (2) the instep joint where the strap is tied. Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and which is preferred here.
The preferred definition for this ruling is the second (instep) based on Imam Muhammad's narration via Hisham.
4
Apply the preferred interpretation to the cutting requirement
Understand that cutting below the ka'bayn means cutting below the instep joint, not the ankle. This affects how the khuff is altered.
The difference matters practically: cutting at the ankle leaves too much fabric and may not fulfill the condition.
5
Contrast with the definition of ka'b in wudu
The commentary notes that in the wudu verse (to the ka'bayn), the first interpretation (ankle) is meant. Recognize that the same word can have different meanings in different legal contexts.
This illustrates the principle that words are interpreted based on context and usage in the Shariah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الحج اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم کہ جو تیاں نہ پائے تو ان کو کسمین [کعبین؟] کے نیچے سے کاٹ دے۔ اور ہشام نے امام محمد سے جو روایت کی ہے اس میں ہے کہ کعب یہاں وسط قدم میں تسمہ باندھنے کی جگہ جوڑ بند کا نام ہے۔

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ محرم کے لئے سلا ہوا کپڑا پہنا جائز نہیں ہے مثلا کر تہ، پانجامہ، عمامہ، ٹوپی ، موزے۔ ہاں اگر محرم کے پاس جو تیاں نہ ہوں تو اس کو ایسے موزے پہننے کی اجازت ہے جن کے تعین سے نیچے کے حصہ کو کاٹ دیا گیا ہو۔ اور کعب سے مراد خنہ [کعب؟] نہیں ہے بلکہ وسط قدم کی ہڈی ہے۔ دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهُمَا قَالَ رَجُلٌ يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ ( صلى الله عليه وسلم ) مَا تَأْمُرُنَا أن تَلْبِسَ مِنَ القِيَابِ فِى الْإِحْرَامِ قَالَ لَا تَلْبِسُوا الْقُمَصَ وَلَا السَرَاوِيلَاتِ وَلَا الْعَمَائِمَ وَلَا الْبَرَانِسَ وَلَا الْحِفَافِ إِلَّا أنْ یَکُونَ أَحَدٌ لَيْسَ لَهُ نَعْلَانِ فَلْيَلْبِسِ الْحُقِّيْنِ وَلْيَقْطَعْ أَسْفَلَ مِنَ الْكَعْبَيْنِ وَلَا تَلْبِسُوا شَيْئًا مَسَّهُ زَعْفَرَانُ وَلَا وَرُسُ - یعنی ابن عمر سے مروی ہے کہ ایک شخص نے کہا کہ اے اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کیا آپ ہم کو احرام کی حالت میں کپڑے پہنے کا حکم کرتے ہیں ۔ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ نہ کرتے پہنو، نہ پائجامے، نہ عمامے، نہ ٹوپیاں اور نہ موزے۔ ہاں اگر کسی کے پاس جوتے نہ ہوں تو موزے پہن لے اور ان کو کھبین [کعبین؟] کے نیچے سے کاٹ دے۔ اور ایسی چیز نہ پہنو جس کو زعفران اور ورس ( ایک قسم کی گھاس تل کے مانند ہے جس سے رنگائی کا کام لیتے ہیں) نے چھوا ہو۔ اس حدیث سے ثابت ہو گیا کہ محرم کے لئے متن میں مذکور کپٹروں کا پہننا ممنوع ہے۔ اور ایک مخصوص حالت میں مخصوص قسم کے موزے کا پہنا جائز ہے۔

صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ کعب کی دو تفسیریں کی گئی ہیں: (1 ٹخنہ یعنی قدم کے دونوں طرف ابھری ہوئی ہڈیاں۔ (۲) وسط قدم میں تسمہ باندھنے کی جگہ جہاں انگلیوں کی ہڈیاں مجتمع ہوتی ہیں۔ ہشام نے امام محمد سے یہی روایت کی ہے۔ پس یہاں کعب کی دوسری تغییر [تفسیر؟] مراد ہے۔ اور کتاب الطہارۃ میں أَرْجُلَكُمْ إِلَى الْكَعْبَینِ کی پہلی تفسیر مراد ہے۔
The book of Hajj. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidaya, volume three. That if he does not find sandals, then he should cut them below the ka'bayn. And what Hisham narrated from Imam Muhammad is that ka'b here in the middle of the foot is the place for tying the strap, the name of the joint.

Explanation: The issue is that for a muhrim, wearing sewn clothing is not permissible, such as a shirt, trousers, turban, cap, socks. Yes, if the muhrim does not have sandals, then he is permitted to wear such socks whose lower portion has been cut below the ka'bayn. And by ka'b is not meant the ankle, but rather the bone in the middle of the foot. The proof is this hadith: from Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) that a man said: O Messenger of Allah, what do you command us to wear of garments in ihram? He said: Do not wear shirts, nor trousers, nor turbans, nor hooded cloaks, nor khuff; except if one does not have sandals, then let him wear khuff and cut them below the two ka'bayn. And do not wear anything touched by saffron or wars (a type of grass like sesame used for dyeing). This hadith establishes that it is prohibited for a muhrim to wear the garments mentioned in the text. And in a specific condition, wearing a specific type of khuff is permissible.

The author of Hidaya says: Two interpretations have been given for ka'b: (1) The ankle, i.e., the protruding bones on both sides of the foot. (2) The place for tying the strap in the middle of the foot, where the bones of the toes meet. Hisham narrated this from Imam Muhammad. So here the second interpretation of ka'b is meant. And in the book of Taharah, the verse 'to the ka'bayn' refers to the first interpretation.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hidaya commentary. It addresses the prohibition of sewn garments for a muhrim, with an exception for khuff (socks/leather socks) if no sandals are available, provided they are cut below the ka'bayn. The author then discusses the definition of ka'b, presenting two interpretations: (1) the ankle bones, and (2) the instep joint where the strap is tied. Citing Hisham's narration from Imam Muhammad, the preferred interpretation here is the second, relevant to cutting the khuff. This differs from the definition in the verse of wudu (to the ka'bayn), where the first interpretation applies. The proof is the well-known hadith of Ibn Umar, which explicitly lists prohibited garments and allows khuff with cutting below the ka'bayn. The hadith is a primary source (Sunnah) for the ruling. The commentary follows the order: ruling, exception, definition, proof, and clarification of intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
کعب (ka'b): In this passage, ka'b refers to the instep (middle of foot) where the strap is tied, as per Imam Muhammad's narration.
محرم (muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what must a muhrim do to his khuff if he lacks sandals?
A) Wear them as they are.
B) Cut them below the ka'bayn.
C) Wear them inside-out.
D) Not wear them at all.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of wearing khuff in ihram is conditional upon cutting them below the instep (ka'bayn), which is the preferred Hanafi interpretation.

Covering Face and Head for Male Muhrim – Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on male muhrim face covering

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on face covering for a male muhrim, cite the primary hadith proof, and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i counterarguments.

Core Idea
A male muhrim must keep his face uncovered; the explicit command of the Prophet overrides ambiguous narrations.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute in Hajj: may a male muhrim cover his face? The Hanafi school holds it is prohibited, while the Shafi'i school permits it. We will explore the proofs from both sides and the Hanafi tarjih, emphasizing the weight of the explicit hadith and the principle of sadd al-dhara'i'.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on face and head covering
Identify the Hanafi ruling: a male muhrim cannot cover his face or head. This is based on explicit prohibition.
The ruling applies to both face and head, but the dispute focuses on the face.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its main proof
The Shafi'i school permits face covering. Their proof is the hadith: 'Ihram of a man is in his head, and of a woman in her face.' They also cite the practice of the Prophet covering his face (narration of Uthman).
Understand the logic: if ihram is in the head, only head is inviolable.
3
Analyze the primary Hanafi proof: the hadith of Ibn Abbas
The Prophet's command regarding a deceased muhrim: 'Do not cover his face nor his head.' This is an explicit prohibition that applies by analogy to all muhrims.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear.
4
Examine the Hanafi qiyas argument
A woman does not cover her face in ihram despite the risk of fitna. By stronger reason (awlā), a man should not cover his face since he poses less fitna.
This is a secondary argument supporting the primary proof.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i hadith and the Uthman narration
The Hanafi scholar explains that the Shafi'i hadith only differentiates head covering between men and women, not face. The Uthman narration is interpreted as covering the nose only, not the entire face.
This shows how apparent contradictions are resolved within the madhhab.

Source Text

وَلَا يُغَطّى وَجْهَهُ وَلَا رَأْسَهُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِى يَجُوزُ لِلرَّجُلِ تَعْطِيَةُ الْوَجْهِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ إِحْرَامُ الرَّجُلِ فِى رَأْسِهِ وَإِحْرَامُ المَراً و فِى وَجُهِهَا وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا تُحْمِرُوا وَجْهَهُ وَلَا رَأْسَهُ فَإِنَّهُ يُبْعَثُ يَوْمَ الْقِيمَةِ مُلَبّيًا قَالَ في مُحْرِم تُوقِيَ وَلِأَنَّ الْمَرْأَةَ لَا تُعَطِي وَجْهَهَا مَعَ أَنَّ فِي الْكَشْفِ فِتْنَةٌ فَالرَّجُلُ بِالطَّرِيقِ الْأُولَى وَفَائِدَةً مَارَوَى الْفَرْقُ فِي تَعْطِيَةِ الرَّأْسِ

ترجمہ اور محرم اپنا چہرہ اور اپنا سر نہ ڈھکے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ مرد کے لئے چہرہ کا ڈھکنا جائز ہے، کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرما ہے کہ مرد کا احترام اس کے سر میں ہے اور عورت کا احرام اس کے چہرے میں ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ تم اسر کا چہرہ مت ڈھکو اور نہ اس کا سر۔ کیونکہ یہ قیامت کے روز تلبیہ کہتا ہوا اٹھے گا۔ یہ حدیث آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایسے محرم کے حق میں فرمائی تھی جوہ گیا تھا۔ اور اس لئے کہ عورت اپنا چہرہ نہیں ڈھکے گی باوجود یکہ کھولنے میں فتنہ ہے پس مرد بطریق اولی اپنا چہرہ نہیں ڈھکے گا اور اس کا فائدہ

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم

کتاب الحج
جس کو امام شافعی نے روایت کیا ہے سر ڈھکنے میں فرق کرنا ہے۔ تشریح محرم مرد کے لئے اپنا سر اور چہرہ ڈھکنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ محرم مرد کو اپنا چہرہ ڈھکنا جائز ہے۔ یہی امام مالک اور امام احمد کا قول ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ إِحْرَامُ الرَّجُلِ فِى رَأْسِهِ وَ إِحْرَامُ الْمَرْأَةِ فِي وَجْهَهَا - یعنی مردكا احرام اس کے سر میں ہے اور عورت کا احترام اس کے چہرہ میں ہے۔ حاصل یہ ہوا کہ مرد کا احترام چونکہ اس کے سر میں ہے اس لئے سر کا ڈھکنا جائز نہ ہوگا اور چونکہ اس کے چہرہ میں احرام نہیں ہے اس لیے چہرہ کا ڈھکنا جائز ہوگا۔ اور حضرت عثمان سے مروی ہے اُنَّ النبي كَانَ يُخَمِّرُ وَجْهَهُ وَهُوَ مُحرم یعنی رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم بحالت احرام اپنا چہرہ ڈھک لیا کرتے تھے ۔ ہماری دلیل ابن عباس کی حدیث ہے اُنَّ رَجُلًا وَقَصَتْهُ رَاحِلتُهُ وَهُوَ مُحْرِمُ فَمَاتَ فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم اِغْسِلُوهُ بِمَاءٍ وَسِدْرٍ وَ كَفَنَوْهُ فِي ثَوْبَيْهِ وَلَا تَمُسُّوهُ طِيبًا وَلَا تَحْمِرُوا رَأْسَهُ وَلَا وَجَهَهُ فَإِنَّهُ يَبْعَثُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ مُلاً یعنی ایک آدمی جو حرم تھا اس کی سواری نے اس کی گردن توڑ دی ، چنانچہ وہ مر گیا ، تو رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اس کو بیری کے پتے ڈال کر پکائے ہوئے پانی میں غسل دو اور اس کے دونوں کپڑوں میں اس کو کفناد و اور اس کو خوشبو مت لگاؤ، اور نہ اس کا سر ڈھکو اور نہ اس کا چہرہ ڈھکو ۔ کیونکہ یہ قیامت کے دن تلبیہ کہتا ہوا اٹھے گا۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مردمحرم کو اپنا سر اور چہرہ ڈھکنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت بحالت احرام اپنا چہرہ نہیں ڈھکے گی حالانکہ اس کا چہرہ کھلنے میں فتنہ ہے۔ پس مرد جس کا چہرہ کھلنے میں کوئی فتنہ بھی نہیں ہے بدرجہ اولیٰ اپنا چہرہ نہ ڈھکے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام شافعی کی روایت کردہ حدیث إِحْرَامُ الرَّجُلِ الحدیث کا فائدہ سر ڈھکنے میں مرد اور عورت کے درمیان فرق ظاہر کرنا ہے، یعنی عورت کے لئے اپنا سر ڈھکنا جائز ہے کیونکہ اس کے احرام کا اثر اس کے چہرہ میں ہوتا ہے نہ کہ سر میں ۔ اور مرد کے لئے سر ڈھکنا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کے احرام کا اثر اس کے سر میں ہوتا ہے۔ اور حدیث عثمان کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بحالت احرام اپنی ناک پر ہاتھ رکھا تھا جس کو راوی نے چہرہ ڈھکنا روایت کیا۔ حالانکہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے چہرہ نہ ڈھکا تھا۔ اور قاضی خاں میں ہے کہ ناک پر ہاتھ رکھنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
And he does not cover his face nor his head. Al-Shafi'i said: It is permissible for a man to cover his face because of his (peace be upon him) statement: 'The ihram of a man is in his head, and the ihram of a woman is in her face.' Our proof is his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Do not cover his face nor his head, for he will be raised on the Day of Resurrection saying the talbiyah.' He said this about a muhrim who died. And because a woman does not cover her face although uncovering it is a source of fitna, then a man, by the first principle (awlā), should not cover his face. And the benefit of what al-Shafi'i narrated is to show the difference in covering the head.

Explanation: A male muhrim may not cover his head and face. Al-Shafi'i said a male muhrim may cover his face. This is also the view of Malik and Ahmad. Al-Shafi'i's proof is the hadith: 'The ihram of a man is in his head and of a woman in her face.' The meaning: since a man's ihram is in his head, covering the head is not permissible, but since his ihram is not in his face, covering the face is permissible. It is also narrated from Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to cover his face while in ihram. Our proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) that a man's riding beast broke his neck while he was muhrim, so he died. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Wash him with water and lotus leaves, shroud him in his two garments, do not apply perfume to him, and do not cover his head nor his face, for he will be raised on the Day of Resurrection saying the talbiyah.' This hadith shows that a male muhrim may not cover his head and face. A second proof is that a woman does not cover her face in ihram, although there is fitna in its exposure, so a man with even less fitna should by priority not cover his face. The author of Hidaya says: The hadith narrated by al-Shafi'i only serves to differentiate between men and women regarding covering the head: women may cover their head because their ihram's effect is in their face, while men may not because their ihram's effect is in their head. As for the hadith of Uthman, the answer is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) placed his hand on his nose, which the narrator mistook for covering the face. In Qadi Khan, it is stated that placing the hand on the nose is not objectionable.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school (represented by the author of Hidaya) and Imam al-Shafi'i (along with Malik and Ahmad). The issue is whether a male muhrim may cover his face. The Hanafi position prohibits covering both the face and the head, while the Shafi'i position permits covering the face. The Shafi'i proof is a hadith that states the ihram of a man is in his head and of a woman in her face, implying that only the head is inviolable. The Hanafi response uses a stronger proof: the hadith of Ibn Abbas concerning a muhrim who died, where the Prophet explicitly commanded not to cover his face or head, indicating that uncovered face and head are mandatory. Additionally, a qiyas argument is made: since women do not cover their face in ihram despite the risk of fitna, men with less fitna should certainly not cover theirs. The author of Hidaya resolves the Shafi'i hadith by limiting its application: it only differentiates between men and women regarding head covering, not face covering. The hadith of Uthman, which suggests the Prophet covered his face, is interpreted as covering only his nose, not his entire face, as supported by Qadi Khan. Thus, the Hanafi ruling stands as the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
احرام (ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj/Umrah, with specific prohibitions.
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The chant recited by pilgrims during Hajj/Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi proof that a male muhrim may not cover his face?
A) The hadith that ihram of a man is in his head.
B) The hadith of the deceased muhrim where the Prophet said do not cover his face or head.
C) Consensus of all scholars.
D) Qiyas: men may cover their face because women do.

Key Takeaway
An explicit prohibition in the Sunnah overrides an ambiguous implication; therefore, a male muhrim must keep his face uncovered in the Hanafi school.

Prohibition of Perfume, Oil, and Hair Removal for the Muhrim
Ruling prohibiting perfume, oil, shaving, and beard trimming during ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four prohibited acts for a muhrim and explain the textual evidence (dalil) for each prohibition.

Core Idea
A muhrim must remain unkempt and without perfume — preserving the state of ihram.

This passage from Al-Hidayah lists the acts a muhrim must avoid: applying perfume, using oil, shaving any body hair, and trimming the beard. Each prohibition is supported by a specific proof – the hadith describing the pilgrim as 'sha'ith' (disheveled) and 'tanfil' (without perfume), the Quranic verse against shaving, and an analogy (qiyas) for beard trimming. We will examine each ruling and its evidence to understand the required state of ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four prohibited acts
From the passage, list: (1) touching perfume, (2) applying oil, (3) shaving head or any body hair, (4) trimming the beard.
These are all forbidden during ihram.
2
Locate the evidence for perfume prohibition
The hadith 'al-hajj al-sha'ith al-tanfil' describes the pilgrim as unkempt and without perfume. This is the primary proof. The Hanafi school derives prohibition from this description.
The hadith is ahad, making the ruling zanni in transmission but operative.
3
Analyze the evidence for shaving prohibition
The Quranic verse (2:196) 'Do not shave your heads' is cited. It is a direct command (amr) which indicates prohibition in the context of ihram.
The verse continues with exceptions for sickness, but the text here establishes the general rule.
4
Understand the qiyas for beard trimming
Trimming the beard is prohibited by analogy to shaving because it also removes hair and eliminates the required state of sha'ath (unkemptness). The common illah (effective cause) is the removal of hair in a way that violates the pilgrim’s state.
This qiyas is a clear application of reasoning by analogy.
5
Recognize the underlying rationale
All these prohibitions aim to maintain the pilgrim's state of humility, dishevelment, and lack of adornment. The passage emphasizes that a muhrim should be free from perfumes and with unkempt hair, signifying detachment from worldly concerns.
Understanding the spirit helps in applying the rule to analogous situations (e.g., modern perfumed products).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا يَمُس طيبًا لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الْحَاجَ الشَّعِثُ التَّنْفِلُ وَكَذَا لَا يَدَّهِنُ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا وَلَا يُحَلِقُ رَأْسَهُ وَلَا شَعَرَ بَدَنِهِ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَلَا تَحْلِقُوا رُءُ وَسَكُم .. الآية وَلَا يَقُصُّ مِنْ لِحْيَتِهِ لِأَنَّهُ فِى مَعْنَى الْحَلْقِ وَلِأَنَّ فِيهِ إِزَالَةٌ الشَّعِثِ وَقَضَاءَ التَّفْث

ترجمہ اور خوشبو نہ لگائے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ حاجی بغیر خوشبو لگائے پراگندہ غبار آلود بالوں والا ہے۔ اور اسی طرح تیل استعمال نہ کرے۔ اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے اور اپنا سر اور اپنے بدن کے بال نہ مونڈے کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اپنے سروں کو نہ مونڈو اور نہ اپنی داڑھی گتر و۔ اس لئے کہ یہ بھی مونڈنے کے معنی میں ہے اور اس لئے کہ اس کی پراگندگی اور میل کچیل کو دور کرتا ہے۔ تشریح محرم خوشبو نہ لگائے ۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے الْحَاجُ الشَّعِثُ النَّفَل شَعِتُ ، شین کے فتحہ اور عین کے کسرہ
He said: And he should not touch perfume, because of his (peace be upon him) statement: 'The pilgrim is disheveled and unadorned.' Likewise, he should not apply oil, due to what we have narrated. And he should not shave his head nor any hair of his body, because of the statement of Allah Most High: 'And do not shave your heads...' [the verse]. And he should not trim his beard, because it is in the meaning of shaving, and because it removes the unkemptness and fulfills the tahallul (ritual completion).

Translation: And he should not apply perfume because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: The pilgrim is disheveled and unadorned. Similarly, he should not use oil, due to the hadith we narrated. And he should not shave his head nor the hair of his body because Allah Most High said: 'And do not shave your heads.' And he should not trim his beard because it is like shaving and it removes the unkemptness and removes the filth. Explanation: A muhrim should not apply perfume because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The pilgrim is disheveled and unadorned.' (Sha'ith: with fat-ha on shin and kasra on 'ayn).
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Quran and Sunnah. It lists prohibitions for a muhrim: applying perfume (based on the hadith describing the pilgrim as disheveled and without perfume), applying oil (by analogy or specific narration), shaving the head or any body hair (based on the Quranic verse from Surah al-Baqarah, 2:196, which partially prohibits shaving before the sacrificial offering), and trimming the beard (by qiyas to shaving, as it also removes the required state of dishevelment). The Hanafi position holds these acts as prohibited (haram) during ihram, and their deliberate commission without valid excuse necessitates a penalty (dam or sadaqah), though the text does not elaborate on penalties here. The proof for perfume is the hadith 'al-hajj al-sha'ith al-tanfil', describing the pilgrim as unkempt (sha'ith) and without perfume (tanfil). The proof for shaving is the explicit Quranic command. The text follows the sequence: prohibition of perfume, then oil, then hair removal, each with its evidence.

Key Terms
الشعث (al-sha'ath): Disheveled, unkempt, with dusty hair; a desired state for a pilgrim.
التنفل (al-tanful): Without perfume; the state of not applying perfume.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for prohibiting perfume during ihram according to this passage?
A) A Quranic verse from Surah al-Baqarah.
B) The hadith describing the pilgrim as 'sha'ith' and 'tanfil'.
C) Analogy (qiyas) to the prohibition of shaving.
D) Consensus (ijma) of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
A muhrim must avoid perfume, oil, shaving, and beard trimming to preserve the state of unkempt humility (sha'ath) required in ihram.

Covering the Face for a Male Muhrim: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i on covering face for male muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a male muhrim covering his face and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Hanafi rebuttal.

Core Idea
A male muhrim must not cover his face — the Prophet's explicit command overrides analogies about the head.

In this lesson, we examine a well-known dispute between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i school regarding whether a male pilgrim in ihram may cover his face. The Hanafi position prohibits both head and face covering, while Imam al-Shafi'i permits face covering. We will trace the proofs of each school and see how the Hanafis rebut the opposing arguments, relying on a clear prophetic directive and a powerful qiyas.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: it is not permissible for a male muhrim to cover his head or his face. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and the majority of the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i (along with Malik and Ahmad) holds that a male muhrim may cover his face, though not his head. Note the precise point of disagreement: the face alone.
The head is agreed upon as prohibited.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: the hadith 'Ihram of a man is in his head, and ihram of a woman is in her face' and the report from Uthman that the Prophet covered his face in ihram.
These suggest that the prohibition is exclusive to the head for men.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school interprets the first hadith as only differentiating head covering between men and women, not addressing the face. The Uthman report is explained as the Prophet placing his hand on his nose, not covering his entire face.
The Hanafi relies on the explicit command in the hadith of Ibn Abbas prohibiting both head and face.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis forbid face covering; Shafi'is allow it. The mufta bihi in al-Hidayah is the Hanafi position.
This difference affects the validity of acts and fidyah obligations.

Source Text

جس کو امام شافعی نے روایت کیا ہے سر ڈھکنے میں فرق کرنا ہے۔ تشریح محرم مرد کے لئے اپنا سر اور چہرہ ڈھکنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ محرم مرد کو اپنا چہرہ ڈھکنا جائز ہے۔ یہی امام مالک اور امام احمد کا قول ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ إِحْرَامُ الرَّجُلِ فِى رَأْسِهِ وَ إِحْرَامُ الْمَرْأَةِ فِي وَجْهَهَا - یعنی مردكا احرام اس کے سر میں ہے اور عورت کا احترام اس کے چہرہ میں ہے۔ حاصل یہ ہوا کہ مرد کا احترام چونکہ اس کے سر میں ہے اس لئے سر کا ڈھکنا جائز نہ ہوگا اور چونکہ اس کے چہرہ میں احرام نہیں ہے اس لیے چہرہ کا ڈھکنا جائز ہوگا۔ اور حضرت عثمان سے مروی ہے اُنَّ النبي كَانَ يُخَمِّرُ وَجْهَهُ وَهُوَ مُحرم یعنی رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم بحالت احرام اپنا چہرہ ڈھک لیا کرتے تھے ۔ ہماری دلیل ابن عباس کی حدیث ہے اُنَّ رَجُلًا وَقَصَتْهُ رَاحِلتُهُ وَهُوَ مُحْرِمُ فَمَاتَ فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم اِغْسِلُوهُ بِمَاءٍ وَسِدْرٍ وَ كَفَنَوْهُ فِي ثَوْبَيْهِ وَلَا تَمُسُّوهُ طِيبًا وَلَا تَحْمِرُوا رَأْسَهُ وَلَا وَجَهَهُ فَإِنَّهُ يَبْعَثُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ مُلاً یعنی ایک آدمی جو حرم تھا اس کی سواری نے اس کی گردن توڑ دی ، چنانچہ وہ مر گیا ، تو رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اس کو بیری کے پتے ڈال کر پکائے ہوئے پانی میں غسل دو اور اس کے دونوں کپڑوں میں اس کو کفناد و اور اس کو خوشبو مت لگاؤ، اور نہ اس کا سر ڈھکو اور نہ اس کا چہرہ ڈھکو ۔ کیونکہ یہ قیامت کے دن تلبیہ کہتا ہوا اٹھے گا۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مردمحرم کو اپنا سر اور چہرہ ڈھکنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت بحالت احرام اپنا چہرہ نہیں ڈھکے گی حالانکہ اس کا چہرہ کھلنے میں فتنہ ہے۔ پس مرد جس کا چہرہ کھلنے میں کوئی فتنہ بھی نہیں ہے بدرجہ اولیٰ اپنا چہرہ نہ ڈھکے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام شافعی کی روایت کردہ حدیث إِحْرَامُ الرَّجُلِ الحدیث کا فائدہ سر ڈھکنے میں مرد اور عورت کے درمیان فرق ظاہر کرنا ہے، یعنی عورت کے لئے اپنا سر ڈھکنا جائز ہے کیونکہ اس کے احرام کا اثر اس کے چہرہ میں ہوتا ہے نہ کہ سر میں ۔ اور مرد کے لئے سر ڈھکنا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کے احرام کا اثر اس کے سر میں ہوتا ہے۔ اور حدیث عثمان کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بحالت احرام اپنی ناک پر ہاتھ رکھا تھا جس کو راوی نے چہرہ ڈھکنا روایت کیا۔ حالانکہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے چہرہ نہ ڈھکا تھا۔ اور قاضی خاں میں ہے کہ ناک پر ہاتھ رکھنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
That which Imam Shafi'i has narrated is a differentiation in covering the head. Explanation: For a male muhrim, covering his head and face is not permissible. Imam Shafi'i said that covering the face is permissible for a male muhrim. This is also the view of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. Imam Shafi'i's proof is the hadith: 'The ihram of a man is in his head, and the ihram of a woman is in her face.' That is, a man's ihram is in his head, and a woman's ihram is in her face. The conclusion is that since a man's ihram is in his head, covering the head is not permissible, and since there is no ihram in his face, covering the face is permissible. It is narrated from Uthman that the Prophet used to cover his face while in ihram. Our proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: a man fell from his mount while in ihram and died. The Messenger of Allah said: Wash him with water and sidr, shroud him in his two garments, do not touch him with perfume, and do not cover his head or his face, for he will be raised on the Day of Resurrection saying the talbiyah. This hadith shows that a male muhrim cannot cover his head or face. The second proof is that a woman does not cover her face in ihram, even though there is fitnah in revealing her face. So a man, whose face being uncovered does not create fitnah, should all the more not cover his face. The author of al-Hidayah says that the hadith narrated by Shafi'i (i.e., 'the ihram of a man is in his head') only demonstrates the difference between men and women in covering the head: meaning that it is permissible for a woman to cover her head because the effect of her ihram is in her face, not in her head. For a man, covering the head is not permissible because the effect of his ihram is in his head. The response to the hadith of Uthman is that the Prophet placed his hand on his nose while in ihram, and the narrator reported it as covering the face, but he did not actually cover his face. In Qadikhan, it is stated that there is no harm in placing the hand on the nose.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether a male muhrim may cover his face. The Hanafi position is that both head and face covering are prohibited. Imam Shafi'i, along with Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad, holds that only the head is prohibited, while the face may be covered. Shafi'i relies on the hadith "Ihram of a man is in his head, and ihram of a woman is in her face," arguing that since the prohibition relates to the head, the face is not included. He also cites a practice of Uthman suggesting the Prophet covered his face. The Hanafi response uses two proofs: first, the hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet explicitly forbids covering both the head and face of a deceased muhrim, indicating both are prohibited. Second, qiyas: a woman in ihram does not cover her face despite greater fitnah, so a man, with less fitnah, should a fortiori not cover his face. Al-Hidayah interprets Shafi'i's hadith as differentiating between men and women regarding the head only, not the face. The hadith of Uthman is explained away as the Prophet covering only his nose with his hand, not his whole face. The relied-upon Hanafi ruling is that a male muhrim must not cover his head or face.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for hajj or umrah.
احرام (ihram): The state of ritual consecration for hajj or umrah, with specific prohibitions.
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The proclamation made by pilgrims during ihram: 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a male muhrim covering his face?
A) It is permissible
B) It is not permissible
C) It is disliked but allowed
D) It is required

Key Takeaway
A male muhrim must not cover his face, as established by an explicit prophetic command in the hadith of Ibn Abbas.

Prohibitions of Perfume and Hair Removal for Muhrim
Ruling on prohibition of perfume, oil, and hair cutting for muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four prohibitions for a muhrim (perfume, oil, shaving head/body hair, trimming beard) and identify the evidence for each prohibition.

Core Idea
A muhrim must remain sha'ith and tafl—any act removing dishevelment is haram.

This passage from al-Hidayah explains the ruling on perfume, oil, and hair removal during ihram. The prohibition is rooted in the hadith describing the pilgrim as disheveled and unperfumed, and in the Quranic command not to shave the head. Trimming the beard is included by analogy. Understanding these prohibitions helps maintain the state of ihram.

Guided Path
1
List the prohibited acts
Identify the four specific acts the author prohibits for a muhrim: applying perfume, applying oil, shaving head/body hair, and trimming the beard.
The passage starts with 'He said: And he should not...' listing each.
2
Locate the evidence for each
For perfume and oil, the proof is the hadith 'al-hajju al-sha'ithu al-tafl'. For shaving, the proof is Quran 2:196 'Do not shave your heads'. For trimming the beard, the proof is analogical reasoning (qiyas) to shaving.
The author also mentions oil is prohibited by what they narrated, likely the same hadith.
3
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
How does the evidence prohibit the act? The hadith describes the pilgrim as 'sha'ith' (disheveled) and 'tafl' (unperfumed); this implies the pilgrim must avoid perfume and maintain dishevelment. The Quran directly prohibits shaving the head. Trimming beard is prohibited because it is 'fi ma'na al-halq' (similar to shaving) and removes dishevelment.
Understanding the 'illa' (effective cause) is key.
4
Apply the reasoning to oil
Oil is prohibited by analogy to perfume because it also makes the hair appear groomed and removes the 'sha'ath' state. The same hadith is used as a general indication.
This shows the Hanafi method of qiyas.

محرم کے لئے خوشبو لگانا اور بال کاٹنا ممنوع ہے
قَالَ وَلَا يَمُس طيبًا لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الْحَاجَ الشَّعِثُ التَّنْفِلُ وَكَذَا لَا يَدَّهِنُ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا وَلَا يُحَلِقُ رَأْسَهُ وَلَا شَعَرَ بَدَنِهِ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَلَا تَحْلِقُوا رُءُ وَسَكُم .. الآية وَلَا يَقُصُّ مِنْ لِحْيَتِهِ لِأَنَّهُ فِى مَعْنَى الْحَلْقِ وَلِأَنَّ فِيهِ إِزَالَةٌ الشَّعِثِ وَقَضَاءَ التَّفْث

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم

It is prohibited for the muhrim to apply perfume and cut hair. He said: And he should not apply perfume because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'The hajj is (for) the disheveled, unperfumed.' Likewise, he should not apply oil because of what we have narrated. And he should not shave his head nor the hair of his body because of the saying of Allah Most High: 'And do not shave your heads...' the verse. And he should not trim his beard because it is similar to shaving and because it removes dishevelment and eliminates dirt. Translation: And do not apply perfume because the Prophet said: 'The hajj is (for) the disheveled, unperfumed.' Similarly, do not use oil because of this hadith which we have narrated. And do not shave your head or body hair because Allah has said: 'Do not shave your heads.' And do not trim your beard because it is equivalent to shaving and because it removes dishevelment and dirt. Explanation: A muhrim should not apply perfume because the Prophet said: 'The hajj is (for) the disheveled, unperfumed.' Shakith: with fatha on shin and kasra on 'ayn, meaning disheveled and dusty hair. And tafl: with fatha on ta and kasra on fa, meaning not applying perfume. So the pilgrim is one with disheveled, dusty hair and no perfume on his hair. For this hadith, oil should not be used. And he should not shave his head or body hair because Allah says: 'Do not shave your heads.' And he should not trim his beard because it is equivalent to shaving and because shaving and cutting removes the dishevelment that is desired for the pilgrim.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that a muhrim must not apply perfume or oil, nor shave or cut any hair from the head, body, or beard. The proof for perfume is the hadith 'al-hajju al-sha'ithu al-tafl' (the pilgrim is disheveled and unperfumed), which describes the desired state. For shaving, the Quranic verse 'wa la tahliku ru'usakum' (do not shave your heads) during hajj is cited. Trimming the beard is analogized to shaving. The explanation emphasizes that the purpose is to maintain a state of dishevelment (sha'ath) and remove traces of refinement. Thus, any action that removes dishevelment, such as cutting hair, is prohibited.

Key Terms
شَعِث (sha'ith): Disheveled, dusty, unkempt hair.
التَّفْل (al-tafl): Unperfumed, without application of perfume.

Key Takeaway
A muhrim must refrain from perfume, oil, shaving, and trimming to maintain the state of dishevelment (sha'ath) and lack of perfume (tafl) prescribed by the Prophet.

Wearing Dyed Garments in Ihram: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute on wearing garments dyed with wars, saffron, or safflower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wearing garments dyed with wars, saffron, or safflower during ihram and explain the basis of the dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
A muhrim cannot wear dyed garments if they retain fragrance; the dispute hinges on whether safflower has a scent.

In this lesson, we examine a classic disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding a muhrim's attire. The key is not the dye's color but its fragrance. The Hanafi school holds that safflower (usfur) has a pleasant scent, thus prohibited, while Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees. The Prophet's hadith permits only washed garments with no scent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wearing a garment dyed with wars, saffron, or safflower during ihram. The Hanafi ruling is that it is prohibited (haram) unless the garment is washed until no scent remains.
The prohibition is due to fragrance, not color.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's hadith: 'The muhrim should not wear a garment touched by saffron or wars unless it is washed so that it does not give off fragrance.' This is a dalil naqli from the Sunnah.
The hadith explicitly excludes washed garments.
3
Analyze the condition
The exception (ghasil) indicates that if the garment is washed thoroughly and no scent remains, it becomes permissible even if the color remains. The cause of prohibition is the scent.
In Hanafi usul, the 'illa (effective cause) is fragrance.
4
Identify the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that safflower-dyed garments are permissible because safflower has no perfume; it is merely a color. Thus, his school allows it unconditionally.
The disagreement is factual: does safflower have a scent?
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school asserts that safflower does have a pleasant scent, therefore it falls under the general prohibition. This is based on empirical observation and the authority of the madhhab.
Both schools agree on the principle; the difference is in the factual assessment.

رنگا ہوا کپڑا پہنے کا حکم
قَالَ وَلَا يَلْبَسُ تَوَبًا مَصْبُوعًا بِوَرْسٍ وَلَا زَعْفَرَانَ وَلَا عُصْفَرَ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا يَلْبِسُ المُحِرمَ ثوبًا مَسه زَعْفَرَانَ وَلَا وَرُسُ إِلا أَنْ يَكُونَ عَسِيلاً لا يَنفِضُ لأنَّ المَنَعَ لِلطَّيبِ لَا لِلَّونِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِي لَا بَاسَ بِلبس المعصْفَر لأنَّه لَوْنُ لَا طِيبَ لَهُ وَلَنَا أَنَّ لَهُ رَائِحَةُ طَيِّبة
ترجمہ اور ورس گھاس ، زعفران اور کم سے رنگا ہوا کپڑا نہ پہنے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ محرم ایسا کپڑا نہ پہلے جس کو زعفران نے چھوا ہو اور نہ ورس نے ، مگر یہ کہ وہ ایسا دھلا ہوا ہو کہ خوشبو نہ دے۔ کیونکہ ممانعت خوشبو کی وجہ سے ہے نہ کہ رنگ کی وجہ سے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ قسم سے رنگا ہوا کپڑ اپنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ ایسا رنگ ہے جس میں خوشبو نہیں ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس میں پاکیزہ خوشبو ہے۔
۔
تشریح ورش والد کا فتہ اور راء کا سکون ہے۔ ایک عمدہ خوشبو دار گھاس ہے جو یمن میں پیدا ہوتی ہے۔ اور شیخ کے قانون میں یہ لکھا ہے کہ ایک سرخ رنگ کی زعفران کی طرح گھاس ہے اور صحاح میں ہے کہ زرد رنگ کی گھاس ہے۔ معصفور، کسم گھاس کا نام ہے ، زرد رنگ ، زعفران تو آپ کو معلوم ہی ہے۔ حاصل مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ محرم کو ایسا کپڑا استعمال کرنا جائز نہیں ہے جو درس یا زعفران یا کم سے رنگا ہوا ہو ۔ کیونکہ رسول اکرم ہے نے فرمایا ہے کہ محرم ایسا کپڑا نہ پینے جس کو زعفران یا درس نے چھوا ہو ۔ چنانچہ صحاح کی کتابوں میں محرم کے بارے میں یہ الفاظ ہیں لا تَلْبَسُوا شَيْنا مَشَهُ وَعَفَرَانٌ وَلَا وَرُسُ - ہاں اگر مذکورہ چیزوں کے ساتھ رنگنے کے بعد اس کو دھوڈالا اور وہ ایسا ہو گیا کہ اس سے خوشبو نہیں آتی ، تو اس کا استعمال جائز ہے اگر چہ رنگ باقی ہو کیونکہ محرم کے لئے خوشبو کا استعمال ممنوع ہے نہ کہ رنگ کا ۔ اور اصل اس میں طحاوی کی ذکر کردہ حدیث ابن عمر ہے قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ لَا تَلَبَسُوا لَوْبًا مَسَّهُ وَرُش أو زعفران إلا أن يكون غسيلاً - ابن عمر نے کہا کہ رسول پاک صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے کہ ورس یا زعفران میں رنگا ہوا کپڑا نہ پہنو مگر یہ کہ اس کو دھوڈالا ہو۔ یا امام شافعی نے کہا کہ کسم میں رنگا ہوا کپڑا محرم کے لئے جائز ہے کیونکہ کسم میں رنگ تو ہوتا ہے مگر خوشبو نہیں ہوتی ۔ اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ ممنوعات احرام میں سے خوشبو سے نہ کہ رنگ ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کسم کے اندر بھی ایک پاکیزہ خوشبو ہوتی ہے۔ ہمارے اور شوافع کے درمیان بنیاد اختلاف یہ ہے کہ شوافع کے نزدیک کسم کے اندر خوشبو نہیں ہوتی اور ہمارے نزدیک خوشبو ہوتی ہے۔
زَعْفَرَانُ إِلَّا
The ruling on wearing a dyed garment. He said: And he should not wear a garment dyed with wars, saffron, or safflower because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'The muhrim should not wear a garment touched by saffron or wars unless it has been washed so that it does not give off fragrance.' Because the prohibition is for perfume, not for color. Shafi'i said: There is no harm in wearing safflower-dyed garment because it is a color that has no perfume. Our proof is that it has a pleasant scent. Translation: And do not wear a garment dyed with wars grass, saffron, or safflower. Because the Prophet said: 'The muhrim should not wear a garment that has been touched by saffron or wars, unless it has been washed so that it gives no fragrance.' Because the prohibition is for perfume, not for color. Shafi'i said: There is no harm in wearing a safflower-dyed garment because it is a color that has no perfume. Our proof is that it has a pleasant scent. Explanation: Wars is an aromatic grass from Yemen. Safflower (usfur) is a plant that gives a yellow color. The conclusion is that a muhrim cannot wear a garment dyed with wars, saffron, or safflower because the Prophet said not to wear anything touched by these. However, if after dyeing it is washed until no fragrance remains, its use is permissible even if color remains, because the prohibition is for perfume. The basis is the hadith of Ibn Umar narrated by Tahawi: 'Do not wear a garment touched by wars or saffron unless it is washed.' Shafi'i said that safflower-dyed garment is permissible because it has no fragrance, but our (Hanafi) evidence is that safflower does have a pleasant scent. The fundamental difference between us and the Shafi'is is that they believe safflower has no scent, while we believe it does.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding wearing garments dyed with certain substances during ihram. The Hanafi ruling, as stated in the matn, prohibits wearing any garment dyed with wars (a fragrant herb), saffron, or safflower (usfur). The proof is the Prophet's prohibition except if the garment is washed so that no fragrance remains, indicating that the prohibition is due to fragrance, not color. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that safflower-dyed clothes are permissible because they lack perfume. The Hanafi response asserts that safflower does have a pleasant scent. The commentary clarifies that the underlying disagreement is factual: whether safflower has a smell. For Hanafis, since it does, it is prohibited. If the garment is washed thoroughly until no scent remains, it becomes permissible even if the color stays. The hadith of Ibn Umar supports this: 'Do not wear a garment touched by wars or saffron unless it is washed.'

Key Terms
ورس (wars): A fragrant herb from Yemen used as a dye.
عصفر (usfur): Safflower, a plant yielding a yellow dye.
غسيل (ghasil): Washed, such that no scent remains.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is it permissible for a muhrim to wear a garment dyed with wars or saffron?
A) When the color is faded
B) When it is washed until no fragrance remains
C) When it is new
D) It is never permissible

Key Takeaway
The prohibition on dyed garments in ihram is based on the presence of fragrance, not the color itself; washed garments without scent are permissible.

Muhrim Bathing and Entering the Bathhouse
Ruling on permissibility of bathing and entering bathhouse for muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a muhrim may bathe and enter a bathhouse, and identify the proof from the practice of Umar (ra).

Core Idea
A muhrim may bathe and enter a bathhouse; the practice of Umar proves it.

A common question for pilgrims is whether they can bathe or use a public bathhouse while in ihram. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position based on a clear precedent from a Companion. You will learn the ruling and the evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules that a muhrim may bathe (ghusl) and enter a public bathhouse (hammam). Determine the hukm level: is it fard, wajib, sunnah, mubah?
The ruling is mubah (permissible).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the action of Sayyiduna Umar (ra): he bathed while in ihram. Identify what kind of evidence this is.
It is an athar (Companion's practice), considered a source of law in the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how Umar's action proves permissibility. The Hanafi principle is that the actions of the Companions (qawl al-sahabi or fi'l al-sahabi) are a proof when not contradicted by stronger evidence.
Since bathing does not violate any ihram prohibition (like perfume or head covering), it remains permissible.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Confirm that the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is permissibility, as stated in Zahir al-Riwayah.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا بَأْسَ بِأَنْ يَغْتَسِلَ وَيَدْخُلَ الْحَمَّامَ لِأَنَّ عُمَرَ اغْتَسَلَ وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ.
He said: There is no harm in his bathing and entering the bathhouse, because Umar bathed while he was a muhrim.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This is a simple ruling statement supported by a proof from the practice of Sayyiduna Umar (may Allah be pleased with him). The matn establishes that a muhrim may perform ghusl (ritual bath) and enter a public bathhouse (hammam). This includes both obligatory ghusl (e.g., for janabah) and recommended ghusl (e.g., before entering Makkah). The hadith narration: Umar ibn al-Khattab performed ghusl while in the state of ihram, as recorded in Muwatta' and other works. This permissibility extends to using hot water, provided no fragrant soap or perfume is applied. The commentary adds that entering the bathhouse is allowed because the Prophet himself performed ghusl in ihram. The prohibition of perfumes remains in effect; the bathhouse itself is not a source of fragrance.

Key Terms
غُسْل (ghusl): Full body wash; here it is permissible whether obligatory or recommended.
حَمَّام (hammam): Public bathhouse, permissible to enter for washing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it permissible for a muhrim to enter the bathhouse according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because it is necessary for hygiene.
B) Because Umar did so while in ihram.
C) Because the Prophet prohibited perfumes, not baths.
D) Because the bathhouse is like a tent.

Key Takeaway
A muhrim may bathe and enter a bathhouse; the action of Umar (ra) provides the primary evidence for this permissibility.

Muhrim Taking Shade: House, Howdaj, and Tent
Inter-madhhab dispute on fustat shade during ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on taking shade for a muhrim and explain why the fustat is permissible, distinguishing it from covering the head.

Core Idea
Shade that does not touch the body is permitted in ihram, even if it covers from above.

When in ihram, a pilgrim must avoid covering the head with something that touches it directly, like a hat or a cloth. But what about shade from a roof, a tent, or a howdaj? This lesson examines a dispute between the Hanafi and Maliki schools, focusing on the large tent (fustat). The Hanafi position is clear: as long as the shade structure does not contact the head, it is permissible.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the matn permits shade from a house (?), mahmal (covered howdaj), and by extension, a fustat.
The matn says 'no harm' in taking shade from these.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam Malik specifically dislikes the fustat and similar structures because they resemble covering the head.
Malik's reasoning is based on qiyas to prohibited head covering.
3
Follow the opponent’s proof
Malik's argument: the fustat covers the head from above, thus resembling a hat or cloth that would be forbidden.
The key point is the resemblance, not actual contact.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis provide two proofs: (1) Athar: Uthman had a fustat pitched in ihram. (2) Qiyas: a fustat does not touch the body, so it is like a house (which is permitted).
The response distinguishes between covering and shading: shade without contact is allowed.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafis allow large tents and canopies during Hajj; Malikis consider them disliked.
The difference affects the fatwa given to pilgrims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا بَأْسَ بِأَنْ يَسْتَظِلَّ بِالْبَيْتِ وَالْمَحْمِلِ وَقَالَ مَالِكٌ يُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَسْتَظِلَّ بِالْفُسْطَاطِ وَمَا أَشْبَهَ ذَلِكَ لِأَنَّهُ يُشَبِهُ تَغْطِيَةَ الرَّأْسِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ عُثْمَانَ كَانَ يُضْرَبُ لَهُ فُسْطَاطٌ فِي إِحْرَامِهِ وَلِأَنَّهُ لَا يَمَسُّ بَدَنَهُ فَأَشْبَهَ الْبَيْتَ.
And there is no harm in his taking shade from a house or a mahmal. Malik said: It is disliked to take shade from a large tent (fustat) and what resembles that, because it resembles covering the head. Our proof is that Uthman had a large tent pitched for him during his ihram, and because it does not touch his body, so it resembles a house.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of taking shade while in ihram. The matn first states a general ruling: it is permissible to seek shade from a house (bayt: any permanent structure) or a mahmal (a howdaj/palanquin on a camel). Imam Malik then raises a specific objection: using a large tent (fustat) or similar structure is makruh because it resembles covering the head, which is prohibited for the muhrim. The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) the practice of Sayyiduna Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) who had a fustat pitched for him while in ihram, and (2) the legal reasoning that a tent does not actually touch the body, so it is analogous to a house, which is permitted. The commentary further cites a hadith from Muslim: during Hajjat al-Wada', Usama and Bilal shaded the Prophet (peace be upon him) with a cloth while he threw the jamrah. This shows that shade that does not directly cover the head is allowed. The key distinction is between shade structures that touch the head (like a hat) and those that provide shade without contact (like a tent or roof). The Hanafi school thus permits the latter.

Key Terms
فُسْطَاط (fustat): A large tent or pavilion used for shade during travel.
مَحْمِل (mahmal): A covered howdaj or litter on a camel, used for carrying passengers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi evidence for allowing the fustat?
A) Analogy to the mahmal.
B) The practice of Uthman.
C) A Quran verse about shade.
D) The Prophet's prohibition of covering the face.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a muhrim may take shade under any structure that does not directly touch the head, including a large tent (fustat).

Bathing and Entering Bathhouse for the Muhrim
States permissibility of bathing and entering bathhouse with proof from Umar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on bathing for a muhrim and identify the proof from Umar ibn al-Khattab.

Core Idea
Bathing is permissible for a muhrim; the action of Umar proves water-based cleaning is not prohibited.

In the state of ihram, many actions are restricted, but purification and hygiene are not among them. This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies that a muhrim may bathe and even enter a bathhouse, provided no prohibited acts like perfuming occur. The proof is the practice of Umar (رضي الله عنه), who bathed while in ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? (bathing / entering bathhouse). What is the expressed ruling? ('la ba'sa' = no harm, hence permissible).
The ruling is mubah (permissible) in general, but can be wajib for janabah or mustahabb for entering Makkah.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The action of Umar (رضي الله عنه) bathing while in ihram. This is a qawl sahabi (saying/action of a companion).
The dalil is from Umar's practice, supported by the fact that the Prophet (ﷺ) did not prohibit it.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does Umar's action prove permissibility? Umar was known for strict adherence; his action shows that bathing is not among the prohibited acts.
The evidence is clear in meaning (dalalah qati'ah) that it is allowed.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there scholarly disagreement? No, this ruling is muttafaq alayh (agreed upon) across madhahib.
No dispute is noted in the source.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Is there a preferred position? The text simply states the ruling without tarjih, as it is the established position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
The mufta bihi is permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا بَأْسَ بِأَن يَعْتَصِلَ وَيَدْخُلَ الْحَمامَ لِأَنَّ عُمَرَ اغْتَسَلَ وَهُوَ مُحْرِم
ترجمہ: اور غسل کرنے اور حمام کے اندر داخل ہونے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ حضرت عمر نے غسل کیا، حالانکہ حضرت عمر محرم تھے۔
تشریح: مسئلہ محرم پر غسل جنابت واجب ہوتا ہے اور مکہ المکرمہ میں داخل ہونے کے لئے غسل کرنا مستحب ہے۔ کیونکہ بحالت احرام رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے غسل کیا ہے۔ اور محرم کے لئے گرم پانی سے غسل کرنے کے واسطے حمام میں داخل ہونے میں بھی کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ حضرت عمر نے محرم ہونے کے باوجود غسل کیا ہے۔
He said: There is no harm in his bathing (ihtisal) and entering the bathhouse, because Umar bathed while he was a muhrim. Translation: And there is no harm in bathing and entering the bathhouse. Because Sayyiduna Umar bathed, although he was a muhrim. Commentary: The issue: Ghusl of janabah is obligatory on a muhrim, and bathing for entering Makkah al-Mukarramah is mustahabb. Because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) bathed while in the state of ihram. And there is no harm in a muhrim entering the bathhouse to bathe with hot water. Because Sayyiduna Umar bathed despite being a muhrim.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The original text (matn) states that there is no harm (la ba'sa) for a muhrim to bathe (ihtisal) and enter a bathhouse. The proof is the action of Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him), who bathed while in ihram. The commentary (sharh) expands this: it clarifies that ghusl for janabah is wajib (obligatory) even for a muhrim, and it is mustahabb to bathe when entering Makkah, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) did. Entering the bathhouse is permissible as long as it does not involve prohibited acts like using perfume. The key point is that water-based cleaning is not prohibited for a muhrim; only certain actions like covering the head or wearing sewn garments are restricted.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): One who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
غسل (ghusl): Full body wash with water, which can be wajib (for janabah) or mustahabb (for entering Makkah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling (hukm) for a muhrim to enter a bathhouse (hamam) according to this passage?
A) Makruh (disliked)
B) Haram (prohibited)
C) Permissible (la ba'sa / no harm)
D) Sunnah (recommended)

Key Takeaway
A muhrim may bathe and enter a bathhouse because water-based cleaning is not restricted in ihram, as proven by the practice of Umar.

Seeking Shade for the Muhrim: Hanafi vs Maliki
Inter-madhhab dispute on seeking shade for the muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on seeking shade for a muhrim and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument using textual and rational proofs.

Core Idea
A muhrim may seek shade from any structure that does not touch the body, like a house; actual head covering is the prohibition.

One of the common questions regarding ihram is what kind of shade is permissible. While it is well-known that a muhrim cannot cover his head, does that include being under a tent? This passage from al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi view that it is fully permissible (mubah), contrasted with the Maliki view that it is disliked (makruh). We will examine the proofs from both sides and understand why the Hanafi school considers it permissible without any dislike.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the act and its ruling: seeking shade from a house, howdah, or large tent is permissible (la ba'sa). Note the explicit statement in the text.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam Malik holds that seeking shade under a large tent (fustat) is makruh because it resembles covering the head. This is a legitimate difference of opinion.
3
Follow the Maliki proof
The Maliki reasoning is based on qiyas (analogy): the tent shades the head, similar to a head covering, which is prohibited. Understand the strength of this analogy.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response provides two proofs: (a) the practice of Uthman (a tent was pitched for him during ihram), and (b) the hadith of the Prophet being shaded by Bilal. Additionally, a rational proof (qiyas jaliy) that a tent does not touch the body, so it is like a house roof.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
For Hanafis, no fidyah is required; the act is mubah. For Malikis, it is makruh but still permissible (no fidyah mentioned). This difference affects the day-to-day practice of pilgrims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا بَأْسَ بِأنْ يَسْتَظِلَّ بِالْبَيْتِ وَالْمَحَمَلٍ وَقَالَ مَالِكُ يُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَسْتَظِلَّ بِالْفُسْطَاطِ وَمَا أَشْبَهَ ذَلِكَ لِأَنَّهُ يُشْبِهُ تَغْطِيَةَ الرَّأْسِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ عُثْمَانَ كَانَ يُضْرَبُ لَهُ فَسْطَاطٌ فِي إحْرَامِهِ وَلِأَنَّهُ لَا يَمَسُّ بَدَنَهُ فَأَشْبَهَ الْبَيْتَ
ترجمہ: اور کوٹھری یا محمل سے سایہ لینے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے اور امام مالک نے فرمایا ہے کہ بڑے خیمہ اور اس جیسی چیز سے سایہ حاصل کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ سر ڈھانکنے کے مشابہ ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت عثمان کے لئے ان کے احرام کی حالت میں بڑا خیمہ نصب کیا جاتا تھا۔ اور اس لئے کہ بڑا خیمہ اس کے بدن کو نہیں چھوتا، اس لئے وہ کوٹھری کے مانند ہو گیا ہے۔
تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک محرم کے لئے چھت اور ہودج وغیرہ سے سایہ حاصل کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بڑے خیمہ سے سایہ حاصل کرنا سرڈھانکنے کے مانند ہے اور پہلے گزر چکا کہ محرم کے لئے سر ڈھانکنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ مگر چونکہ خیمہ سے سایہ حاصل کرنے کی صورت میں حقیقی سر کا ڈھانکنا نہیں ہے اس لئے محرم کے واسطے خیمہ سے سایہ حاصل کرنا ناجائز تو نہ ہوگا البتہ مشابہت کی وجہ سے مکروہ ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عقبہ بن حبان کہتے ہیں کہ میں نے عثمان کو دیکھا کہ ان کے لئے ایک بڑا خیمہ نصب کیا جاتا اور ان کی تلوار درخت میں لٹکا دی جاتی، حالانکہ عثمان محرم ہوتے تھے۔ اور مسلم شریف میں ام حصین کی حدیث ہے: حَجَجْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللهِ حَجَّةَ الْوَدَاعِ فَرَأَيْتُ أُسَامَةَ وَبِلَالًا وَأَحَدُهُمَا آخِذٌ بِخِطَامِ نَاقَةِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ وَالْآخَرُ رَافِعٌ ثَوْبَهُ سِتْرَةً مِنَ الْحَرِّ حَتَّى رَمَى جَمَرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ۔ ام حصین کہتی ہیں کہ ہم نے رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے ساتھ حجتہ الوداع کیا۔ میں نے اسامہ اور بلال کو دیکھا کہ ان میں سے ایک رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی اونٹنی کی نکیل تھامے ہوئے ہے اور دوسرا اپنا کپڑا اٹھا کر رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کو گرمی سے بچانے کے لئے آپ کے سر پر سایہ کئے ہوئے ہے۔ حتی کہ آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کی۔ عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بڑا خیمہ آدمی کے بدن کو نہیں چھوتا، لہذا یہ مکان کی چھت کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ اور مکان کی چھت سے سایہ حاصل کرنے میں چونکہ کوئی کراہت نہیں ہے، اس لئے بڑے خیمہ سے سایہ حاصل کرنے میں بھی کوئی کراہت نہ ہوگی۔
And there is no harm in his seeking shade with the house and the howdah. And Malik said: It is disliked (makruh) to seek shade with the large tent (fustat) and what resembles that, because it resembles covering the head. And our proof is that Uthman used to have a large tent pitched for him during his ihram, and because it does not touch his body, so it resembles the house. Translation: And there is no harm in seeking shade from a room or a howdah. And Imam Malik said that seeking shade from a large tent and similar things is makruh, because it resembles covering the head. And our proof is that a large tent was pitched for Uthman during his state of ihram, and because a large tent does not touch his body, so it becomes like a room. Commentary: The issue is that according to us, it is permissible for a muhrim to seek shade from a roof and a howdah, etc. And Imam Malik's proof is that seeking shade from a large tent is like covering the head, and it has already passed that covering the head is not permissible for a muhrim. But because in seeking shade from a tent there is no actual covering of the head, therefore seeking shade from a tent is not impermissible for a muhrim; however, due to similarity it would be makruh. Our proof is that Uqba bin Hibban said: I saw Uthman, and a large tent was pitched for him, and his sword was hung on a tree, while Uthman was a muhrim. And in Sahih Muslim, the hadith of Umm al-Husayn: We performed Hajjat al-Wada' with the Messenger of Allah. I saw Usamah and Bilal; one of them was holding the rope of the she-camel of the Messenger of Allah, and the other was raising his garment as a screen from the heat until he (the Prophet) threw the Jamrat al-Aqabah. Umm al-Husayn says: We performed Hajjat al-Wada' with the Messenger of Allah. I saw Usamah and Bilal; one of them was holding the reins of the Messenger of Allah's she-camel, and the other was raising his cloth to shade the Prophet's head from the heat until he threw the Jamrat al-Aqabah. The rational proof is that a large tent does not touch a person's body, so it becomes similar to the roof of a house. And since there is no dislike in seeking shade from a house roof, there will be no dislike in seeking shade from a large tent.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi position is that a muhrim may seek shade from a house (bayt) or a howdah (mahmal) without any dislike. Imam Malik, however, considers seeking shade from a large tent (fustat) to be makruh because it resembles covering the head, which is prohibited for a muhrim. The Hanafis respond with two proofs: first, the practice of Uthman ibn Affan (may Allah be pleased with him), who had a large tent pitched for him while he was muhrim. Second, a hadith from Sahih Muslim where the Prophet (peace be upon him) was shaded by Bilal raising his garment during the Hajj. The rational argument is that a tent does not touch the body, so it is analogous to a house roof, which is clearly permissible. Thus, the Hanafi ruling is that it is not makruh. The text also clarifies that Imam Malik's view is based on the similarity to head covering, but because there is no actual covering, it is not prohibited, only potentially makruh. The Hanafi stance is that it is absolutely permissible (la ba'sa).

Key Terms
محمل (mahmal): A howdah or litter carried by a camel, used to transport people.
فسطاط (fustat): A large tent or pavilion made of cloth, capable of providing shade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a muhrim seeking shade under a large tent (fustat)?
A) Haram, because it resembles covering the head
B) Makruh, disliked
C) Permissible, no harm (la ba'sa)
D) Sunnah, recommended

Key Takeaway
A muhrim may seek shade from any structure that does not actually cover the head; this is mubah according to the Hanafi school based on the practice of Uthman and the hadith of the Prophet being shaded.

Entering Under the Kaaba Curtains for the Muhrim
Ruling on muhrim under Kaaba curtains with conditional permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition-based ruling for a muhrim entering under the Kaaba curtains and explain the qiyas to istizlal.

Core Idea
For a muhrim, entering under the Kaaba curtains is permissible only if the cloth does not touch the head or face.

This lesson examines a specific scenario during Hajj: a muhrim seeking shelter under the Kaaba's covering. The text distinguishes between permissible shade and prohibited covering, using the principle of istizlal. Understanding this distinction is crucial for avoiding what resembles a forbidden act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The act is a muhrim entering under the curtains (astar) of the Kaaba. The key condition is whether the curtain touches the head or face.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
If no touch: the ruling is 'la ba'sa' (no harm, mubah). If touch: the ruling is makruh (disliked).
3
Identify the proof (dalil)
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to istizlal (seeking shade), which is generally permissible for a muhrim. The text explicitly says 'because it is seeking shade'.
4
Analyze the analogy (qiyas)
The asl (original case) is seeking shade without head/face contact, which is mubah. The far' (new case) is entering under the Kaaba curtains. The illa (effective cause) is the absence of head/face covering. If contact occurs, the illa changes, making it analogous to covering the head, hence makruh.
5
Note the underlying principle
The principle is that any act that resembles a prohibited act (covering the head) is makruh. Here, direct contact with the head/face transforms permissible shade into disliked covering.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ دَخَلَ تَحْتَ أَسْتَارِ الْكَعْبَةِ حَتَّى غَطَّتْهُ إِنْ كَانَ لَا يُصِيبُ رَأْسَهُ وَلَا وَجْهَهُ فَلَا بَأْسَ لِأَنَّهُ اسْتِظْلَالٌ
ترجمہ: اور اگر محرم کعبہ کے پردوں میں گھس گیا حتی کہ اس کو ڈھانک لیا، پس اگر پردہ اس کے سر اور چہرہ کو نہیں چھوتا تو کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ سایہ لینا ہے۔
تشریح: اگر محرم کعبہ کے پردوں کے نیچے داخل ہو گیا حتی کہ اس کو پردوں نے ڈھانک لیا تو دو صورتیں ہیں۔ اگر پردہ اس کے چہرہ اور سر کو نہیں لگا تو اس میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ سایہ حاصل کرنا ہوا۔ اور سایہ حاصل کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے اور اگر پردہ سر یا چہرہ کو لگ گیا تو مکروہ ہے۔ کیونکہ اب یہ سر ڈھانکنے کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔
And if he enters under the curtains of the Kaaba until they cover him, if they do not touch his head and his face, then there is no harm, because it is seeking shade. Translation: And if a muhrim enters under the curtains of the Kaaba until they cover him, then if the curtain does not touch his head and face, there is no harm, because this is seeking shade. Commentary: If a muhrim enters under the curtains of the Kaaba until the curtains cover him, there are two scenarios. If the curtain does not touch his face and head, then there is no harm, because this is seeking shade, and there is no harm in seeking shade. And if the curtain touches the head or face, then it is makruh, because it then resembles covering the head.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, parsed into two scenarios. The original text (matn) gives a conditional ruling: if a muhrim enters under the curtains (astar) of the Kaaba and they cover him, then if the curtain does not touch his head or face, it is permissible (la ba'sa) because it is merely seeking shade (istizlal). The commentary (sharh) clarifies the second scenario: if the curtain touches the head or face, it becomes makruh (disliked) because it is similar to covering the head, which is prohibited for a muhrim. The underlying principle is that shade itself is permissible, but direct contact with the head or face mimics the prohibited act of covering. This ruling is based on qiyas (analogy) to the general permissibility of shade for a muhrim.

Key Terms
أستار الكعبة (astar al-ka'bah): The curtains or covering (kiswah) of the Kaaba.
استظلال (istizlal): Seeking shade, which is generally permissible for a muhrim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muhrim enters under the Kaaba curtains and the cloth touches his head, what is the ruling?
A) Permissible (mubah)
B) Makruh (disliked)
C) Haram (prohibited)
D) Wajib (obligatory)

Key Takeaway
For a muhrim, the permissibility of entering under the Kaaba curtains depends on whether the cloth touches the head or face; if it does not, it is permissible as seeking shade; if it does, it is makruh due to resemblance to covering.

Tying a Money Belt (Himyan) for the Muhrim: Hanafi Ruling and Maliki Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on tying a money belt for a muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tying a himyan for a muhrim and explain the Hanafi response to the Maliki objection based on necessity.

Core Idea
The himyan is permissible for a muhrim because it is not a sewn garment; necessity is irrelevant.

A pilgrim in ihram may need to carry money for expenses or for others. The Hanafi school unhesitatingly permits tying a money belt (himyan) around the waist, while Imam Malik qualifies it based on necessity. This lesson examines the proofs and the practical consequence of the difference, including a subtle objection that tests the consistency of the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State clearly that the Hanafi school considers tying a himyan permissible (mubah) for a muhrim, whether the money belongs to him or another.
The text opens with 'لا بأس' indicating no prohibition.
2
Understand the Maliki objection
Imam Malik distinguishes based on necessity: if the himyan contains another's money, tying it is makruh because there is no necessity. Identify the basis: necessity as a criterion for permissibility.
Malik's view: necessity makes the action mubah; without necessity, it becomes makruh.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafis argue that the himyan is not in the meaning of wearing sewn garments (makhit), so the prohibition does not apply. They also cite the hadith of Aisha (رضي الله عنها) giving general permission to secure money.
The key phrase: 'ليس في معنى لبس المخيط' – the himyan is not analogous to sewn clothing.
4
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical difference: Hanafis allow the himyan in all cases; Malikis allow only when it contains one's own money.
This affects a pilgrim carrying travel money for a companion.
5
Examine the objection about izaar/rida'
The text raises an objection: tying the izaar or rida' with a rope is makruh by consensus, yet a rope is also not sewn. Similarly, a head bandage is makruh. How can the himyan be different? Think how a Hanafi might respond.
The objection probes the consistency of the proof. A Hanafi response: the rope/bandage substitutes for sewn fastening, whereas the himyan is an accessory, not a garment replacement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا بَأْسَ أَنْ يَشُدَّ فِي وَسَطِهِ الْهَمْيَانَ وَقَالَ مَالِكُ يَكْرَهُ إِذَا كَانَ فِيهِ نَفَقَهُ غَيْرِهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا ضَرُورَةَ وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ فِي مَعْنَى لِبْسِ الْمَخِيطِ فَاسْتَوَتْ فِيهِ الْحَالَتَانِ
ترجمہ: اور اپنی کمر میں ہمیانی باندھنے میں بھی کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے اور امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ اگر اس میں دوسرے کا نفقہ ہو تو مکروہ ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہمیانی باندھنا سلا ہوا کپڑا پہننے کے معنی میں نہیں ہے۔ پس اس کے حق میں دونوں حالتیں برابر ہیں۔
تشریح: ہمیان (بکسر الباء) وہ بٹوا جو بٹوے یا تھیلی کا کام دے، جس میں روپے رکھ کر کمر سے باندھ لیا جاتا ہے۔ ہمارے نزدیک ہمیان کو کمر سے باندھنے میں محرم کے لئے کوئی قباحت نہیں ہے خواہ اس کو ازار کے نیچے باندھے یا ازار کے اوپر باندھے۔ حضرت امام مالک نے فرمایا ہے کہ ہمیانی میں اگر اپنا خرچہ ہو تو اس کو باندھنا بلا کراہت جائز ہے۔ اور اگر دوسرے کا خرچہ اور روپیہ پیسہ ہو تو اس کو باندھنا مکروہ ہے۔ امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہمیانی میں دوسرے کا خرچہ ہو تو اس کو باندھنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں اور بلا ضرورت باندھنا محرم کے لئے مکروہ ہے۔ اور جب اپنا روپیہ پیسہ ہو تو چونکہ اس وقت ضرورت متحقق ہے اس لئے جائز ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہمیان چونکہ سلے ہوئے کپڑے کے معنی میں نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو باندھنے میں کوئی کراہت نہیں ہے خواہ اس میں اپنا خرچہ ہو یا دوسرے کا ہو دونوں حالتیں برابر ہیں۔ اور اصل دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک بار حضرت صدیقہ عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا سے دریافت کیا گیا تھا کہ کیا محرم ہمیانی باندھ سکتا ہے؟ آپ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا نے فرمایا: استوثق في نفقتك بما شئت یعنی اپنے نفقہ اور روپیہ پیسے کی حفاظت جس طرح چاہے کرو۔ اس سے بھی ہمیانی باندھنے کا جواز ثابت ہوا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کی طرف سے پیش کردہ عقلی دلیل پر ایک اشکال ہے۔ وہ یہ کہ محرم کے لئے اپنے ازار اور رداء کو رسی یا ڈورے وغیرہ سے باندھنا بالاجماع مکروہ ہے حالانکہ رسی اور ڈورا سلے ہوئے کپڑے کے معنی میں نہیں ہے۔ اس طرح اگر محرم نے اپنے سر پر پٹی باندھی تو یہ بھی مکروہ ہے حتی کہ کامل ایک دن باندھنے کی صورت میں صدقہ واجب
And there is no harm in his tying the himyan (money belt) around his waist. And Malik said: It is disliked (makruh) if it contains the expenses of another, because there is no necessity. And our proof is that it is not in the meaning of wearing stitched garments, so the two situations are equal. Translation: And there is no harm in tying a himyan around the waist. And Imam Malik said: If it contains the expenses of another, it is makruh, because there is no necessity. And our proof is that tying a himyan is not in the meaning of wearing sewn cloth, so both situations are equal. Commentary: Himyan (with kasra on the ba) is a purse that serves as a wallet or pouch, in which money is kept and tied to the waist. According to us, there is no prohibition for a muhrim in tying the himyan around the waist, whether he ties it under the izaar or over the izaar. Imam Malik said that if the himyan contains one's own expenses, tying it is permissible without dislike. But if it contains the expenses and money of another, tying it is makruh. Imam Malik's proof is that if the himyan contains another's expenses, there is no necessity to tie it, and without necessity it is makruh for a muhrim. When it is one's own money, because necessity is established, it is permissible. Our proof is that the himyan is not in the meaning of sewn cloth, so there is no karahah in tying it, whether it contains one's own expenses or another's; both situations are equal. And the original proof is that once Sayyidah Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) was asked: Can a muhrim tie a himyan? She said: 'Istawthiq fi nafaqatika bima shi'ta' meaning 'Secure your expenses and money as you wish.' This also proves the permissibility of tying the himyan. There is an objection to the rational proof presented by the author of Hidayah: For a muhrim, tying his izaar and rida' with a rope or string is unanimously makruh, even though the rope and string are not in the meaning of sewn cloth. Similarly, if a muhrim ties a bandage on his head, this is also makruh, to the extent that if he ties it for a complete day, sadaqah becomes wajib...
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute with an additional objection. The Hanafi position is that a muhrim may tie a himyan (money belt) around his waist without any dislike (la ba'sa), regardless of whether the money inside is his own or another's. Imam Malik distinguishes: if the himyan contains his own expenses, it is permissible; if it contains another's, it is makruh due to lack of necessity. The Hanafis argue that the himyan is not like wearing sewn garments (makhit), so it does not fall under the prohibition. They also cite the response of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her), who told a questioner to secure his money as he wishes. An objection is raised: if tying a himyan is permissible even though it resembles a belt, then why is tying the izaar (lower garment) or rida' (upper garment) with a rope makruh by consensus? The objector extends this to tying a bandage on the head, which is also makruh. The text cuts off before the Hanafi response, but the implication is that there is a difference between a belt for money and a rope used to secure clothing that could be seen as an alternative to wearing sewn garments. The Hanafi position remains that the himyan is permissible.

Key Terms
ہمیان / الهميان (himyan / al-himyan): A money belt or purse tied around the waist to carry money.
مخيط / المَخِيط (makhit / al-makhit): Sewn or stitched garments, which are prohibited for a muhrim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a muhrim ties a himyan (money belt) containing another person's money?
A) Makruh, because there is no necessity
B) Haram, because it is like assisting in a sin
C) Permissible, the same as if it were his own money
D) Wajib, if the owner entrusted him

Key Takeaway
The himyan is permissible for a muhrim because it is not a sewn garment; the Hanafi school rejects the necessity distinction.
