Touching the Black Stone with an Object When Direct Contact is Not Possible
Ruling on touching the Black Stone with an object and kissing it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on touching the Black Stone with an object when direct contact is not possible, explain the graded substitute actions, and cite the prophetic proof.

Core Idea
Use a stick to touch the Stone and kiss the stick — prophetic substitute when direct istilam is impossible.

When performing tawaf, kissing or touching the Black Stone is a beloved sunnah. But what if crowds or distance prevent direct contact? This passage from the Hanafi tradition provides a clear, graded solution: touch the Stone with an object, kiss that object, and if even that is not possible, simply face the Stone and recite. Let's explore the ruling and its proof from the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? It is the act of touching the Black Stone with an object and kissing that object. The hukm is sunnah muakkadah – a confirmed sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith: the Prophet performed tawaf on his mount and used a crooked staff (mihjan) to make istilam of the corners. This shows permissibility and desirability.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of using an object for istilam indicates that this is a valid substitute when direct touch is not feasible. The ruling is derived from the precedent (ta'sis al-mashru'iyyah).
4
Note the gradation
The text presents a sequence: first try direct touch with hand/lips; if impossible, use an object and kiss it; if that is also impossible, face the Stone and recite the prescribed dhikr.
This gradation ensures the sunnah is preserved as much as possible.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school follows this graded approach, as found in the zahir al-riwayah. It is universally accepted within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حجر اسود کو کسی بھی چیز سے چھونا ممکن ہو تو چھولے
قَالَ وَإِنْ أَمْكَنَهُ أَنْ يَمَسَّ الْحَجَرَ بِشَيْءٍ فِي يَدِهِ كَالْعَرْجُونِ وَغَيْرِهِ ثُمَّ قَبَّلَ ذَلِكَ فَعَلَهُ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ طَافَ عَلَى رَاحِلَتِهِ وَاسْتَلَمَ الْأَرْكَانَ بِمِحْجَنِهِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ شَيْئًا مِنْ ذَلِكَ اسْتَقْبَلَهُ وَكَبَّرَ وَهَلَّلَ وَ حَمِدَ اللهَ وَصَلَّى عَلَى النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ
ترجمہ کہا کہ اگر حجر اسود کو ایسی چیز سے چھونا ممکن ہو جو اس کے ہاتھ میں ہے جیسے شاخ وغیرہ پھر اس کو بوسہ دے دے تو وہ ایسا کر لے۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اپنی سواری پر طواف کیا اور اپنی چھڑی سے ارکان کا استلام فرمایا۔ اور اگر ان امور میں سے کسی بات پر قادر نہ ہو تو حجر اسود کا استقبال کرے اور اللہ اکبر کہے اور لا الہ الا اللہ کہے اور اللہ کی حمد کرے اور آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پر درود پڑھے۔ تشریح حدیث میں لفظ محجن نون کے کسرہ اور جیم کے فتحہ کے ساتھ آیا ہے۔ ٹیڑھے سروالے ڈنڈے کو کہتے ہیں۔ جیسے آج کل بوڑھے حضرات ہاتھ میں چھڑی رکھتے ہیں۔ بہر حال مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر حجر اسود کو بوسہ دینا یا ہاتھ سے چھونا ممکن نہ ہو تو بصورت امکان یہ کرے کہ اپنے ہاتھ میں لکڑی لے کر اس کو حجر اسود سے مس کرے پھر اس لکڑی کو چوم لے۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے طواف کیا اور اپنے ہاتھ میں موجود چھڑی سے ارکان یعنی حجر اسود اور رکن یمانی کا استلام فرمایا۔ اور اگر اس کی بھی قدرت نہ ہو تو حجر اسود کے سامنے کھڑا ہو کر اللہ اکبر کہے ، لا اله الا اللہ کہے اور اللہ کی حمد بیان کرے۔ اور اللہ کے رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پر درود پڑھے۔
He said: And if he can touch the Stone with something in his hand, like a branch or other, then kiss that object, he should do so, because of the narration that he (peace be upon him) performed tawaf on his mount and made istilam of the corners with his crooked staff. And if he is unable to do any of that, he should face it, say takbir, tahlil, praise Allah, and send blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him). Translation: He said: If it is possible to touch the Black Stone with something that is in his hand, like a branch etc., then he should give it a kiss, so he does that. Because it is narrated that the Messenger of Allah performed tawaf on his mount and made istilam of the corners with his staff. And if he is not able to do any of these things, then he should face the Black Stone, say Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illallah, praise Allah, and send blessings on the Prophet. Commentary: In the hadith, the word 'mihjan' comes with kasra on the nun and fatha on the jim. It refers to a crooked stick, like today's elderly people hold a staff. In any case, the ruling is that if kissing the Black Stone or touching it with the hand is not possible, then if possible, he should take a stick in his hand, touch the Black Stone with it, then kiss that stick. Because it is narrated that the Prophet performed tawaf and made istilam of the corners - the Black Stone and the Yemeni Corner - with a stick in his hand. And if he is not able to do even that, then he should stand facing the Black Stone, say Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illallah, praise Allah, and send blessings on the Messenger of Allah.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage deals with the further gradation of istilam when direct contact with the Black Stone is not possible. It presents a ruling with proof: if the pilgrim cannot touch the Stone with his hand or kiss it, he may use an object (like a stick or branch) to touch the Stone and then kiss that object. This is based on the prophetic practice of performing tawaf on his mount and using a crooked staff (mihjan) to make istilam of the corners. If even that is not possible (e.g., no object available, or the crowd prevents any contact), then the pilgrim simply faces the Stone, says takbir and tahlil, praises Allah, and sends salawat upon the Prophet. The commentary explains the term 'mihjan' and emphasizes that this is the sequence of options: direct touch, touch with an object, or facing and recitation. This shows the Hanafi school's detailed gradation of acts, ensuring that even when the preferred sunnah cannot be performed, a substitute is available to maintain the ritual connection.

Key Terms
محجن (miḥjan): A crooked stick or staff used by the Prophet to touch the Black Stone during tawaf on his mount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a pilgrim cannot touch the Black Stone with his hand, what is the first recommended substitute?
A) Use an object to touch the Stone and kiss the object.
B) Face the Stone and recite takbir.
C) Wait until the crowd clears.
D) Skip istilam entirely.

Key Takeaway
When direct touch is impossible, the Hanafi school permits touching the Black Stone with an object and kissing it, based on the Prophet's use of a mihjan.

The Sunnah of Idtiba' and the Manner of Starting Tawaf
Ruling on idtiba' and starting tawaf from the door side

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of idtiba' in the Hanafi school, explain its definition, and apply the sunnah method when performing tawaf.

Core Idea
Idtiba' is a sunnah muakkadah for men, not wajib; its omission does not invalidate tawaf.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on idtiba'—the practice of uncovering the right shoulder during tawaf. The passage from Al-Hidayah establishes that idtiba' is a sunnah (recommended) act, proven by the Prophet's own practice. Understanding this ruling helps you perform tawaf correctly, following the sunnah without overburdening yourself with unnecessary obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is idtiba' (placing the cloak under the right armpit and over the left shoulder). The passage states it is a sunnah (sunna). In Hanafi terminology, this means a highly recommended practice, not obligatory.
Sunnah muakkadah is the category here, though the text simply says 'sunna'.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the narrated action of the Prophet (peace be upon him): he performed istilam of the Black Stone, then moved to his right side near the door, and completed seven circuits while having made idtiba'.
The dalil is a hadith (ahad) regarding the Prophet's actual practice in tawaf.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's specific actions (istilam, moving right, idtiba', seven circuits) establish the method and the recommendation. The phrase 'wa huwa sunna' directly indicates the ruling.
The proof is direct (dalil naqli) and not based on qiyas.
4
Note ikhtilaf and application
There is no significant intra-Hanafi or inter-madhhab disagreement on idtiba' being sunnah. The practical takeaway: men should practice idtiba' during tawaf of 'umrah and hajj; women do not.
The ruling is muttafaq alayh (unanimous across schools that it is sunnah).

اضطباع کا حکم
قَالَ ثُمَّ أَخَذَ مِنْ يَمِينِهِ مِمَّا يَلِي الْبَابَ وَقَدِ اضْطَبَعَ رِدَاءَهُ فَيَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ اسْتَلَمَ الْحَجَرَ ثُمَّ أَخَذَ عَنْ يَمِينِهِ مِمَّا يَلِي الْبَابَ فَطَافَ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ وَالْإِضْطِبَاعُ أَنْ يَجْعَلَ رِدَاءَهُ تَحْتَ إِبِطِهِ الْأَيْمَنِ وَيُلْقِيَهُ عَلَى كَتِفِهِ الْأَيْسَرِ وَهُوَ سُنَّةٌ وَقَدْ نُقِلَ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ
ترجمہ کہا کہ پھر اپنے دائیں طرف جہاں سے متصل دروازہ ہے شروع کرے حال یہ کہ وہ اپنی چادر کا اضطباع کر چکا ہے۔ پس خانہ کعبہ کے گردسات چکر لگائے ۔ کیونکہ روایت ہے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حجر اسود کا استلام کیا پھر اپنی دائیں جانب سے جو دروازہ کے متصل ہے شروع کیا۔ پس سات پھیرے طواف کیا۔ اور اضطباع یہ ہے کہ اپنی چادر کو اپنی دائیں بغل کے نیچے سے نکال کر اپنے بائیں مونڈھے پر ڈالے۔
Ruling on idtiba': He said: Then he takes from his right side, next to the door, while he has made idtiba' of his cloak, so he performs tawaf around the House seven circuits, because of the narration that he (peace be upon him) made istilam of the Stone, then took from his right side, next to the door, and performed tawaf seven circuits. And idtiba' is that he places his cloak under his right armpit and throws it over his left shoulder, and it is a sunnah, and it has been transmitted from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). Translation: He said: Then he starts from his right side, where it is adjacent to the door, while he has made idtiba' of his cloak. So he circumbulates the Kaaba seven circuits. Because it is narrated that the Prophet made istilam of the Black Stone, then started from his right side, which is adjacent to the door, and performed tawaf of seven circuits. And idtiba' is that he takes his cloak from under his right armpit and throws it over his left shoulder.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on idtiba' (wearing the upper garment with the right shoulder exposed) during tawaf. It begins by stating that after making istilam of the Black Stone, the pilgrim should start tawaf by moving to his right, heading towards the door of the Kaaba (i.e., the direction where the door is located). He should already have performed idtiba' of his shawl or cloak. Idtiba' is defined as placing the garment under the right armpit and throwing the ends over the left shoulder, thus baring the right shoulder. This is a sunnah act, proven by the practice of the Prophet during his farewell pilgrimage. The proof cited is that the Prophet made istilam of the Black Stone, then proceeded from his right side next to the door and completed seven circuits. Thus, the Hanafi ruling emphasizes that idtiba' is a sunnah for men during tawaf, and the starting point is from the direction of the door after istilam.

Key Terms
اضطباع (iḍṭibāʿ): A manner of wearing the upper garment during tawaf by placing it under the right armpit and throwing the ends over the left shoulder, exposing the right shoulder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Fold the cloak and place it on the head.

Key Takeaway
Idtiba' is a sunnah muakkadah for men during tawaf; it is recommended but not obligatory, and its omission does not affect the validity of tawaf.

Ruling on Touching the Black Stone (Istilam)
Extends ruling on touching Black Stone with substitutes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istilam, explain its sunnah status, and identify the conditions under which alternatives are permitted.

Core Idea
Istilam is sunnah, but avoiding harm is wajib — sunnah cannot override wajib.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on touching the Black Stone (istilam) during Tawaf. While it is a beloved sunnah of the Prophet, the school emphasizes that it must not cause harm to others. We will see the proofs from the Prophet's practice and the hierarchy of alternatives when direct touching is difficult.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State that istilam of the Black Stone is sunnah muakkadah in the Hanafi school. Note that it is not wajib or fard.
The ruling is based on ahad hadith and the principle of avoiding harm.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the hadith where the Prophet performed Tawaf on his mount and touched the corners with a crooked staff (mihjan). Also the instruction to Umar not to crowd the stone.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim, transmitted as ahad.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of using a staff shows that indirect touching is permissible. The instruction to Umar establishes that causing harm is prohibited, creating a hierarchy: sunnah is waived if it conflicts with wajib.
The Dalil block in this lesson elaborates on the proof.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other madhahib consider istilam wajib. The Hanafi school holds it as sunnah due to the zanni nature of the dalil and the overriding principle of avoiding harm.
The Hanafi position box provides details on this.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi position is that istilam is sunnah; if it causes harm, one faces the stone and makes dhikr. This is the relied-upon view in the Hidayah.
The tarjih authority is Al-Marghinani.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم کتاب الج اقرار کو پتھر میں ودیعت رکھ دیا۔ پس جو شخص اس کا استلام کرتا ہے گویا وہ اس اقرار کے ساتھ تجدید عہد کرتا ہے اور پتھر کل قیامت میں اس کے لئے شہادت دے گا ۔ ( عنایہ ) بہر حال کسی مسلمان کو اذیت پہنچائے بغیر اگر ممکن ہو تو ضرور حجر اسود کا استلام کرے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ نے حجر اسود کو بوسہ دیا۔ اور اس پر اپنے ہونٹ رکھے۔ اور حضرت عمر سے فرمایا کہ تو ایک مرد قوی ہے کمزور کو ایذا . دے گا اس لئے حجر اسود پرلوگوں سے مزاحم نہ ہونا یعنی از دحام کو نہ ہٹانا ورنہ کمزور کو تجھ سے ایذاء پہنچے گی لیکن اگر جگہ خالی ہو اور بھیڑ بھاڑ نہ ہوتو استلام کر لینا، یعنی منہ یا ہاتھ سے چھو لینا۔ اور اگر گنجائش نہ ہو بلکہ بھیڑ ہو، تو اس کے سامنے کھڑے ہو کر تکبیر و تجلیل کر لینا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ استلام سنت ہے اور مسلمان کو ایذاء دینے سے بچنا واجب ہے۔ اور سنت ادا کرنے کے لئے واجب ترک کرنے کی شرعا قطعاً اجازت نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے مسلمان کو ایذاء پہنچائے بغیر اگر استلام ممکن ہو تو استلام کرے دور نہ تو استقبال پر اکتفاء کرے۔

حجر اسود کو کسی بھی چیز سے چھونا ممکن ہو تو چھولے

قَالَ وَإِنْ أمْكَنَهُ أن يمس الْحَجَرَ بِشَيْءٍ فِي يَدِهِ كَالْعَرْجُونِ وَغَيْرِهِ ثُمَّ قَبَّلَ ذَلِكَ فَعَلَهُ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السّلامُ طَافَ عَلَى رَاحِلَتِهِ وَاسْتَلَمَ الْأَرْكَانَ بِمِحْجَنِهِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ شَيَا مِنْ ذَلِكَ اسْتَقْبَلَهُ وَكَبَّرَ وَهَلَّلَ وَ حَمِدَ اللهَ وَصَلَّى عَلَى النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ

ترجمہ کہا کہ اگر حجر اسود کو ایسی چیز سے چھوناممکن ہو جو اس کے ہاتھ میں ہے جیسے شاخ وغیرہ پھر اس کو بوسہ دے دے تو وہ ایسا کر لے۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنی سواری پر طواف کیا اور اپنی چھڑی سے ارکان کا استلام فرمایا۔ اور اگر ان امور میں سے کسی بات پر قادر نہ ہو تو حجر اسود کا استقبال کرے اور اللہ اکبر کہے اور لا الہ الا اللہ کہے اور اللہ کی حمد کرے اور آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم پر درود پڑھے ۔ تشریح حدیث میں لفظ محجن نیم کے کسرہ اور جیم کے فتحہ کے ساتھ آیا ہے۔ ٹیڑھے سروالے ڈنڈے کو کہتے ہیں۔ جیسے آج کل بوڑھے حضرات ہاتھ میں چھڑی رکھتے ہیں۔ بہر حال مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر حجر اسود کو بوسہ دینا یا ہاتھ سے چھو نا ممکن نہ ہو تو بصورت امکان یہ کرے کہ اپنے ہاتھ میں لکڑی لے کر اس کو حجر اسود سے مس کرے پھر اس لکڑی کو چوم لے۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے طواف کیا اور اپنے ہاتھ میں موجود چھٹڑی سے ارکان یعنی حجر اسود اور رکن یمانی کا استلام فرمایا۔ اور اگر اس کی بھی قدرت نہ ہو تو حجر اسود کے سامنے کھڑا ہو کر اللہ اکبر کہے ، لا اله الا اللہ کہے اور اللہ کی حمد بیان کرے۔ اور اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم پر درود پڑھے۔
Ashraf al-Hidaya, commentary Urdu of Hidaya, volume three, Kitab al-Hajj. Regarding depositing in a stone: so whoever performs istilam of it, it is as if he renews the covenant with that acknowledgment, and the stone will bear witness for him on the Day of Judgment. (Inayah) In any case, without causing harm to any Muslim, if possible, he should definitely perform istilam of the Black Stone. Because the Messenger of Allah kissed the Black Stone and placed his lips on it. And he said to Umar: 'You are a strong man; you will harm the weak. Therefore, do not crowd people at the Black Stone, i.e., do not remove congestion, otherwise the weak will be harmed by you.' But if the place is empty and there is no crowding, then he may perform istilam, i.e., touch it with his mouth or hand. And if there is no capacity, rather there is crowding, then standing facing it, he should say takbir and glorify. The second proof is that istilam is sunnah and avoiding harm to a Muslim is obligatory. And for performing a sunnah, it is absolutely not permitted by Shariah to abandon an obligatory act. Therefore, if istilam is possible without harming a Muslim, he should do istilam, otherwise he should suffice with facing it.

If it is possible to touch the Black Stone with anything, he should touch it.

He said: And if it is possible for him to touch the stone with something in his hand, like a palm branch or other, then if he kisses that, he should do so. Because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed Tawaf on his mount and touched the corners with his crooked staff. And if he is not able to do any of that, he should face it and say Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illallah, praise Allah, and send blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Translation: He said: If it is possible to touch the Black Stone with something in his hand, like a branch etc., and then he kisses it, then he should do so. Because it is narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed Tawaf on his mount and touched the corners with his stick. And if he is not able to do any of these things, he should face the Black Stone and say Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illallah, praise Allah, and send blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him). Explanation: The word 'mihjan' in the hadith appears with a kasrah on the meem and a fatha on the jeem. It refers to a crooked stick, like the staff that elderly people carry today. In any case, the ruling is that if kissing the Black Stone or touching it with the hand is not possible, then if possible, he should take a piece of wood in his hand, touch it to the Black Stone, and then kiss that wood. Because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed Tawaf and touched the corners, i.e., the Black Stone and the Yamani corner, with a stick he had in his hand. And if he is not able to do even that, then he should stand facing the Black Stone and say Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illallah, praise Allah, and send blessings on the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a ruling with proof regarding the istilam (touching) of the Black Stone (Hajar al-Aswad) during Tawaf. The author first establishes the significance of istilam by relating that it is like a renewal of a covenant with Allah and that the stone will bear witness. He then presents the ruling: it is sunnah to touch the Black Stone with one's mouth or hand, but this is conditioned upon not harming any Muslim. If there is crowding and causing harm is likely, then one should not push through, but rather face the stone and recite takbir and tahmid. The rationale is that avoiding harm to a Muslim is obligatory (wajib), and performing a sunnah cannot justify abandoning a wajib. The author then quotes the matn of Hidayah, which provides the alternative: if direct touching is not possible, one may use an object (like a palm branch or stick) to touch the stone, and then kiss that object, based on the Prophet's action of touching the corners with a crooked staff while riding. If even that is not possible, one simply faces the stone and makes dhikr. The commentary elaborates on the word 'mihjan' and reiterates the hierarchy of actions. The overall message is that the sunnah of istilam should be performed as fully as possible, but never at the expense of causing harm.

Key Terms
استلام (istilam): Touching the Black Stone with the hand or mouth as an act of reverence during Tawaf.
حجر اسود (hajar al-aswad): The Black Stone set in the eastern corner of the Kaaba, kissed during Tawaf.
محجن (mihjan): A crooked staff or stick used for touching the stone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Push through the crowd to touch the Stone because it is sunnah.
B) Use a long stick to touch the Stone from a distance.
C) Face the Stone and say takbir and tahmid.
D) Wait until the crowd disperses, even if it takes hours.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, istilam of the Black Stone is a sunnah that must be abandoned if it leads to harming others, because avoiding harm is wajib and takes precedence.

Manner of Tawaf: Idtiba' and Starting from the Right
Describes sunnah of Idtiba' and obligation to start Tawaf from the right.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the obligation of starting Tawaf from the right and the sunnah of idtiba', and identify the consequence of performing reverse Tawaf.

Core Idea
Starting Tawaf from the right is wajib; reversing it requires repetition or dam.

In this passage, the author explains two key aspects of Tawaf: the sunnah act of idtiba' (uncovering the right shoulder) and the obligation to start the circumambulation from the right side, adjacent to the door. The proof is the Prophet's practice. The passage also clarifies the serious consequence of reversing the direction—a reverse Tawaf that must be corrected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
Determine what is ruled upon: idtiba' (sunnah) and starting from the right (wajib). Note the hukm level for each.
Idtiba' is sunnah muakkadah; starting from the right is wajib.
2
Examine the dalil
The proof cited is the Prophet's action: he touched the Black Stone and then moved to his right. In Hanafi methodology, the Prophet's consistent actions in worship indicate obligation (wajib).
The hadith is ahad, providing zanni proof.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The operative part is the Prophet's starting from the right adjacent to the door. Since it was done deliberately and repeatedly, it establishes a binding practice.
Hanafi usul: the Prophet's actions in ibadat are obligatory unless evidence shows otherwise.
4
Apply the ruling: consequence of violation
If one starts from the left (reverse Tawaf), the ruling depends on location: if still in Makkah, repeat; if returned home, a dam is wajib. This shows the act is wajib, not rukn.
Repetition is required for validity; dam compensates if repetition is impossible.

اضطباع کا حکم

قَالَ ثُمَّ أَخَذَ مِن يَمِينِهِ مِمَّا لِي الْبَابَ وَقَدْ اضْطَبَعَ رِدَانَهُ فَيَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ لِمَارُوِىَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلام اِستَلَمَ الْحَجَرَ ثُمَّ أَخَذَ عَنْ يَمِينِهِ مِمَّايلى الْبَابَ فَطَافَ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ وَالْإِصْطِبَاعُ أَنْ يَجْعَلَ رِدَاء تَحْتَ إِبِطِهِ الْأَيْمَنِ وَيُلْقِيْهَ عَلَى كَتِفِهِ الْأَيْسَرَ وَهُوَ سُسَةً وَقَدْ نُقِلَ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ

ترجمہ کہا کہ پھر اپنے دائیں طرف جہاں سے متصل دروازہ ہے شروع کرے حال یہ کہ وہ اپنی چادر کا اضطباع کر چکا ہے۔ پس خانہ کعبہ کے گردسات چکر لگائے ۔ کیونکہ روایت ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حجر اسود کا استلام کیا پھر اپنی دائیں جانب سے جو دروازہ کے متصل ہے شروع کیا۔ پس سات پھیرے طواف کیا۔ اور اضطباع یہ ہے کہ اپنی چادر کو اپنی دائیں بغل کے نیچے سے نکال کر اپنے بائیں مونڈھے پر ڈال

کتاب الحج
۳۲۴
لے۔ اور اضطباع سنت ہے اور اضطباع کرنا رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے منقول ہے۔

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم

تشریح مسئلہ - طواف جس طرح حجر اسود سے شروع کرنا واجب ہے اسی طرح دائیں جانب سے طواف کرنا واجب ہے۔ یعنی حجر اسود سے دائیں جانب جہاں سے دروازہ متصل ہے، اس جانب سے طواف کرنا شروع کرے۔ حالانکہ اگر بجائے دائیں جانب سے شروع کرنے کے بائیں جانب سے طواف شروع کیا اور اسی طرح سات شوط کر ڈالے تو یہ طواف معکوس ( الٹا طواف ) کہلائے گا۔ ہمارے نزدیک اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ جب تک مکہ میں ہے اس کا اعادہ کرے۔ اور اگر اعادہ سے پہلے ہی لوٹ کر اپنے وطن چلا گیا تو اس پر دم واجب ہوگا۔ بہر حال طواف حجر اسود سے دائیں جانب کو شروع کرے اور اسی طرح سات شوط پورے کرے کیونکہ رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بھی اسی طرح طواف کیا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اضطباع ، ضبع بمعنی بازو سے ماخوذ ہے اور اس کی کیفیت یہ ہے کہ اپنی چادر کو اپنے دائیں بغل کے نیچے سے نکال کر اس کو بائیں کندھے پر ڈالے۔ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ درویشانہ ہیئت مسنون ہے اور رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم سے منقول ہے۔
The Ruling on Idtiba'

He said: Then he starts from his right side, which is adjacent to the door, while he has performed idtiba' of his cloak. So he circumambulates the House seven circuits. Because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) touched the Black Stone, then started from his right side adjacent to the door, and performed seven circuits. And idtiba' is that he places his cloak under his right armpit and throws it over his left shoulder. And it is sunnah, and it has been transmitted from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).

Translation: He said: Then he starts from his right side, which is adjacent to the door, while he has performed idtiba' of his cloak. So he circumambulates the Kaaba seven circuits. Because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) touched the Black Stone, then started from his right side adjacent to the door, and performed seven circuits. And idtiba' is that he takes his cloak out from under his right armpit and places it on his left shoulder. And idtiba' is sunnah, and performing idtiba' is transmitted from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).

Ashraf al-Bidayah, commentary of Urdu of Hidayah, volume three

Explanation of the issue: Just as it is wajib to start Tawaf from the Black Stone, similarly it is wajib to perform Tawaf from the right side. That is, from the Black Stone, the right side adjacent to the door, he should start the Tawaf. However, if instead of starting from the right side, he starts Tawaf from the left side and performs seven circuits in that manner, then this is called 'ma'kus' (reverse Tawaf). In our school, its ruling is that as long as he is in Makkah, he should repeat it. And if he returns to his homeland before repeating, then a dam (sacrifice) becomes obligatory upon him. In any case, he should start Tawaf from the Black Stone to the right side and completes seven circuits in that manner because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) also performed Tawaf in this way. The author of Hidayah says: Idtiba' is derived from 'dhab' meaning arm, and its manner is that he takes his cloak out from under his right armpit and places it on his left shoulder. He says that this mendicant-like posture is sunnah and is transmitted from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the manner of Tawaf, specifically the sunnah of idtiba' (wearing the cloak under the right armpit and over the left shoulder) and the wajib of starting Tawaf from the right side adjacent to the door. The author begins by quoting the matn: after touching the Black Stone, the pilgrim should proceed to the right side (towards the door) and perform seven circuits, while having performed idtiba'. The proof is the Prophet's action. Then the commentary elaborates that starting from the right is wajib (obligatory), and if one mistakenly starts from the left and does a reverse Tawaf, the ruling is that if still in Makkah, he must repeat the Tawaf; if he has left Makkah, a dam (sacrificial animal) becomes wajib. The explanation also clarifies that idtiba' is sunnah and describes its form: the middle of the cloak is placed under the right armpit, and the ends are thrown over the left shoulder, leaving the right shoulder bare. This is specifically for men during Tawaf with ramal. The author notes that this is a transmitted practice from the Prophet.

Key Terms
اضطباع (idtiba'): To place the cloak under the right armpit and throw it over the left shoulder, leaving the right shoulder uncovered, during Tawaf.
طواف معكوس (tawaf ma'kus): Reverse Tawaf performed in the opposite direction (starting from left instead of right), which is invalid and must be repeated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim starts Tawaf from the left side (the corner opposite the door) and completes seven circuits, what does Hanafi fiqh require?
A) The Tawaf is valid, but he should repeat it out of caution.
B) He must repeat the Tawaf if still in Makkah; otherwise, a dam is wajib.
C) The Tawaf is valid and no compensation is needed.
D) He should perform two rak'ahs of nafl prayer as compensation.

Key Takeaway
Starting Tawaf from the right side adjacent to the door is a wajib in Hanafi fiqh; deliberate reverse Tawaf requires repetition or a dam.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
Tawaf Must Be Performed Outside the Hatim
Establishes Tawaf must be outside Hatim with proof and secondary prayer ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tawaf in relation to the Hatim, explain the proof from the hadith of Aisha, and justify why prayer facing only the Hatim is invalid.

Core Idea
The Hatim is part of the Kaaba, so Tawaf must completely encircle it externally.

This lesson addresses a critical detail of Tawaf: the area known as the Hatim (or Hijr). The Hanafi school holds that the Hatim is an integral part of the original Kaaba structure, even though it was left out during the Quraysh rebuilding. Therefore, every circuit of Tawaf must be performed outside the Hatim. The proof comes directly from the hadith of Aisha (ra). We will also explore an important epistemological point: why prayer facing only the Hatim is invalid even though it is part of the Kaaba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Tawaf (circumambulation of the Kaaba). The ruling is that it must be performed outside the Hatim. If any part of the Tawaf is inside the Hatim, that circuit is invalid.
The Hatim is the semi-circular area adjacent to the Kaaba containing the mizab.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Aisha (ra) in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The Hatim is from the House.' This establishes that the Hatim is part of the Kaaba.
This hadith is a solitary report (khabar wahid), but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Since the Hatim is part of the Kaaba, the obligation to circumambulate the Kaaba means one must go around both the main structure and the Hatim. Entering the Hatim would mean short-circuiting the Tawaf.
Thus, Tawaf must be from outside the entire original perimeter.
4
Note the secondary ruling on prayer
The author contrasts Tawaf with prayer: facing only the Hatim for prayer is invalid. The reason is that the qibla obligation is based on definitive Qur'anic texts (nass al-kitab), whereas the Hatim's inclusion is from a solitary hadith. For matters of fundamental obligation, one cannot rely on a non-definitive proof.
This shows the Hanafi principle of caution (ihtiyat) in applying weaker evidence to matters of established certainty.
5
Apply the Hanafi principle of caution
In Tawaf, caution dictates staying outside the Hatim to ensure the act is valid. In prayer, caution dictates not using the solitary hadith to override the Qur'anic qibla obligation.
Both rulings reflect the same principle: where there is a conflict between a definitive and a non-definitive proof, the definitive takes precedence.

طواف حطیم کے باہر سے کرے

قَالَ وَيَجْعَلَ طَوَافَهُ مِنْ وَرَاءِ الْحَظِيمِ وَهُوَ اسْمٌ لِمَوْضِعُ فِيهِ الْمِيزَابُ يُسَمَّى بِهِ لِأَنَّهُ حَطِمَ مِنَ الْبَيْتِ أَى كُسِرَ، وَسُمِّيَ حَجرًا لأنَّهُ حُجرَمِنْهُ وَهُوَمِنَ المَيْتِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ فِى حَدِيثِ عَائِشَةَ فَإِنَّ الْعَظِيمَ مِنَ الْبَيْتِ فَلِهذَا يَجْعَلُ الطَّوَافَ مِنْ وَرَائِهِ حَتَّى لَوْ دَخَلَ الْفَرْجَةَ الَّتِي بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الْبَيْتِ لَا يَجُوزُ إِلَّا انه إذا اسْتَقْبَلَ الْحَظِيم وَحْدَهُ لا يُجْزِيْهِ الصَّلوة لأنَّ فَرِضِيَّةَ التَّوَجُهِ ثَبَتَ بِنَصِ الْكِتَابِ فَلا يَتَادَى بِمَا ثَبَتَ بِخَيْرِ الْوَاحَدِ اِحْتِيَاطَاً وَالاحْتِيَاطُ فِي الطَّوَافِ أَنْ يَكُونَ وَرَاءَ هُ

ترجمہ کہا کہ اور شخص اپنے طواف کو حطیم کے باہر کرے اور حطیم ایک جگہ کا نام ہے جس میں میزاب رحمت واقع ہے۔ اس کا نام حطیم اس لئے ہوا کہ بیت میں سے نظم یعنی تو ڑا گیا ہے ( اور اس کا نام حجر بھی ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ بیت اللہ سے مجور یعنی ممنوع کیا گیا ۔ حالانکہ بیت اللہ کا حصہ ہے) کیونکہ حدیث عائشہ میں ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ حطیم بیت میں سے ہے۔ پس اسی وجہ سے طواف حطیم کے باہر سے کیا جائے گا۔ حتی کہ طواف کرنے والا اگر اس کشادگی میں داخل ہوا جو عظیم اور بیت کے درمیان ہے تو جائز نہیں لیکن اگر مصلی نے فقط حطیم کا استقبال کیا تو نماز جائز نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ استقبال قبلہ کی فرضیت نص کتاب سے ثابت ہے۔ پس احتیاطاً اس سے ادا نہیں ہوگا جس کا ثبوت خبر واحد سے ہوا۔ اور طواف کے اندر احتیاط یہ ہے کہ حطیم سے باہر ہو۔

تشریح حطیم اس جگہ کا نام ہے جس میں میزاب رحمت واقع ہوا ہے۔ حطیم کو حطیم اس لئے کہا جاتا ہے کہ حکم کے معنی توڑنے کے ہیں۔ اور مشرکین مکہ نے بیت اللہ کی تعمیر نو کے وقت خرچ کی کمی کی وجہ سے اس حصہ کو توڑ کر بیت اللہ کی تعمیر نو میں شامل نہیں کیا تھا ۔ حطیم کا دوسرا نام حجر ( بكسر الحاء) ہے۔ جس کے معنی روکنے کے ہیں یعنی اس حصہ کو بیت اللہ کی تعمیر نو میں شامل کرنے سے روک دیا گیا تھا۔ لیکن یہ خیال رہے کہ حطیم ، بیت اللہ کا ایک حصہ ہے جو احکام بیت اللہ کے ہیں وہی حطیم کعبہ کے ہیں۔ اس پر حدیث عائشہ شاہد عدل ہے۔ مصاحب عنایہ نے جو حدیث ذکر کی ہے اس کا ترجمہ یہ ہے کہ عائشہ نے یہ نذر کی تھی کہ اگر مکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم پر فتح ہو گیا تو بیت اللہ میں دو رکعت نماز پڑھیں گی۔ پس (فتح مکہ کے بعد ) رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت عائشہ کا ہاتھ پکڑ کران کو حطیم کعبہ میں داخل کیا اور فرمایا صلی
He should make his Tawaf from outside the Hatim. And Hatim is a name for the place in which the waterspout (mizab) is located. It is called hatim because it was broken from the House, i.e., shattered. And it is called hijr because it was prevented from it, and it is part of the House, because of his statement (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Aisha: 'Indeed the Hatim is from the House.' Therefore, Tawaf should be performed from its outside. So much so that if the person performing Tawaf enters the gap between it and the House, it is not permissible. However, if a worshipper faces only the Hatim, his prayer will not suffice him, because the obligation of facing the qibla is established by the text of the Book, so it cannot be fulfilled by what is established by a solitary report, out of caution. And caution in Tawaf is to be outside it.

Translation: He said: And the person should make his Tawaf from outside the Hatim. And Hatim is the name of a place in which the water spout (mizab al-rahmat) is located. It is named Hatim because it was broken from the House, i.e., shattered. (And it is also called Hijr because it was prevented from the House of Allah, even though it is a part of the House). Because in the hadith of Aisha, the Messenger of Allah said: 'The Hatim is from the House.' Therefore, for this reason, Tawaf should be performed from outside it. So much so that if the person performing Tawaf enters the gap that is between it and the House, it is not permissible. But if a worshipper (musalli) faces only the Hatim, his prayer will not be valid. Because the obligation of facing the qibla is established by the text of the Book, so it will not be fulfilled by what is established by a solitary report, out of caution. And caution in Tawaf is to be outside it.

Explanation: Hatim is the name of the place where the water spout (mizab al-rahmat) is located. Hatim is called hatim because the meaning of 'hatm' is 'break'. And the polytheists of Mecca, at the time of rebuilding the House, due to lack of funds, broke this portion and did not include it in the rebuilding. The other name of Hatim is Hijr (with kasr of ha). The meaning of which is 'to prevent', i.e., this portion was prevented from being included in the rebuilding of the House. But it should be noted that the Hatim is a part of the House of Allah, and the same rulings apply to it as to the Kaaba. The hadith of Aisha is a just witness for this. The hadith mentioned by the author of 'Inayah' is: Aisha vowed that if Mecca is conquered by the Messenger of Allah, she would pray two rak'ahs inside the House. So after the conquest, the Messenger of Allah took Aisha's hand, entered her into the Hatim, and said: 'Pray'
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling that Tawaf must be performed outside the Hatim (also called Hijr). The author explains that the Hatim is a semi-circular area adjacent to the Kaaba, which originally was part of the House but was left out during the Quraysh's rebuilding due to lack of funds. The proof is the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that the Hatim is from the House. Therefore, one cannot perform Tawaf inside the Hatim; the entire Tawaf must be outside it. If someone goes inside the Hatim during Tawaf, that part of the Tawaf is invalid. The author also draws a parallel with prayer: if a person prays facing only the Hatim (i.e., not towards the actual Kaaba), the prayer is not valid because the obligation of facing the qibla is established by the Qur'an, while the fact that the Hatim is part of the Kaaba is established by a solitary hadith (khabar wahid). Since the qibla is based on definitive evidence (Qur'an), it cannot be determined by a non-definitive proof. Hence, for caution, the Tawaf must be outside the Hatim.

Key Terms
حطيم (hatim): The semi-circular area adjacent to the Kaaba containing the water spout (mizab), which is part of the original structure of the House.
حجر (hijr): An alternative name for the Hatim, meaning 'prevented' because it was left out of the Kaaba's rebuilding.
ميزاب (mizab): The water spout (golden downspout) that drains rainwater from the roof of the Kaaba, located above the Hatim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is prayer facing only the Hatim (and not the entire Kaaba) not valid?
A) Because the Hatim is not part of the Kaaba.
B) Because the obligation of qibla is based on the Qur'an, while the Hatim's status is from a solitary hadith.
C) Because prayer is not allowed near the Hatim.
D) Because the Hatim is used for water drainage and is impure.

Key Takeaway
The Hatim is part of the Kaaba; therefore Tawaf must be performed outside it, and prayer facing only the Hatim is invalid.
